Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Conditions and Procedure of Li'an
Defines li'an and its procedure with proofs and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that necessitate li'an, explain its procedure as established in the Quran and Sunnah, and evaluate the Hanafi position on when judicial separation occurs.

Core Idea
Li'an is a wajib procedure that substitutes the hadd penalty; separation only occurs by the judge's ruling after both spouses complete their oaths.

In this lesson, we examine the Islamic institution of li'an (mutual imprecation) as defined and detailed in the Hanafi school. Li'an is the procedure when a husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses, and it serves as a substitute for the hadd penalty. We will explore the conditions that trigger li'an, the exact oath procedure derived from Surah al-Nur, and a key scholarly dispute: when exactly does the marriage dissolve? Understanding this procedure is essential for correctly applying a ruling that balances the rights of both spouses and upholds the sanctity of marital bonds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon (li'an) and its legal classification (wajib). Note the conditions that make li'an applicable or exempt the husband.
The passage begins with conditions when no hadd or li'an is required.
2
Locate the Primary Dalil
Identify the Quranic verses (Surah al-Nur 24:6-9) and the Prophetic practice (hadith of Hilal and 'Uwaymir) that establish the procedure. Recognize that the text explicitly cites both.
The dalil is qat'i al-thubut (Quran) and the Sunnah (hadith).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the imperatives in the Quran and the actions of the Prophet specify the exact wording and sequence of oaths for the husband and wife. Note the reliance on indirect reference (isharah) in zahir al-riwaya.
The phrase 'اشهد بالله إني لمن الصادقين' directly indicates the oath form.
4
Analyze the Inter-Madhhab Dispute on Timing of Separation
State the Hanafi position (separation by judge's ruling after both complete li'an) and the opposing views (immediate separation after husband's oaths). Identify the proofs used by each side.
The thamarah al-khilaf is crucial: inheritance rights if one dies before judge's ruling.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi school adopts the requirement of a judge's ruling: the hadith of 'Uwaymir divorcing after li'an, and the practice of the Prophet explicitly separating them after li'an. Recognize that the opposing hadith is interpreted as a prohibition of cohabitation, not automatic divorce.
The mufta bihi position is that separation is a ba'in talaq, not a permanent prohibition (except in Abu Yusuf's view).

باب اللعان
حد، وإن صلح وهي ممن لا يحدّ قاذفها فلا حدّ عليه ولا لعان. وصفته ما نطق به النص، أي الزوج شاهداً أي المرأة لأنه خلف عن الحد أي كيفية اللعان حد لأن اللعان تعذر معنى من جهته فيصار إلى الموجب الأصلي (ع) قاذفها بأن كانت زانية أو صبية أو نحوهما. (ط، ع) فلا حد عليه أي على الزوج؛ لأنه صادق في القذف لكنه يعزر. (م، ط،ع) لأن امتناع فلا حد عليه ولا لعان لأنها ليست من أهل الشهادة فكان الامتناع لمعنى فيها فلا يوجب الحد، واللعان خلف عنه، وكذا إذا كانت مجنونة أو صغيرة أو محدودة في قذف فلا حد ولا لعان، وإن كانا محدودين في قذف حد؛ عبداً اللعان لمعنى من جهته؛ إذ هو ليس من أهل الشهادة، وكذا إذا كان هو . وهي محدودة في قذف يحد، بخلاف ما إذا كانا كافرين أو مملوكين حيث لا يجب عليه الحد، وإن امتنع من جهته؛ لأن قذف الأمة والكافرة لا يوجب الحد، وقال الشافعي: يلاعن في الكل، إلا إذا كان أحدهما صغيراً أو مجنوناً أو كلاهما، فقد مضى على أصله بكون الزوج أهلا لليمين، ومضينا على أصلنا بكونه أهلاً للشهادة، ثم الإحصان يعتبر عند القذف حتى لو قذفها وهي أمة أو كافرة ثم أسلمت أو عتقت لا يجب الحد ولا اللعان [رمز الحقائق: ٢٩٠/١] ما نطق به النص: أي ما ذكر الله تعالى في هذه الآيات: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ أَزْوَاجَهُمْ (النور:1) إلى قوله تعالى: وَالْخَامِسَةَ أَنَّ غَضَبَ اللهِ عَلَيْهَا إِنْ كَانَ مِنَ الصَّادِقِينَ (النور:۹) واعلم أن سبب نزول الآية أن هلال بن أمية جاء إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقال: غبت عن امرأتي سنتين فلما رجعت وجدت على بطن امرأتي شريك ابن السحماء يزني بها، فقال له علي : " انت بأربعة شهود وإلا تجلد على ظهرك " فقال هلال رأيت بعيني يا رسول الله، وأعاد هذه المقالة ثم قال: وإني لأرجو من الله أن يجعل لي مخرجاً، فأنزل الله هذه الآيات، فدل ذلك على أن اللعان قائم مقام حد القذف في حق الزوج حيث لم يجلد هلال بقذفه وقائم مقام حد الزنا في حق المرأة؛ لأنه عليها قال في آخر الحديث : لولا الأيمان سبقت لكان لي ولها شأن" فينبغي للقاضي أن يبتدئ بالزوج، فيشهد أربع شهادات، يقول في كل مرة: "أشهد بالله إني لمن الصادقين فيما رميتها به من "الزنا" يشير إليها في كل مرة، ويقول في الخامسة: "لعنة الله عليه إن كان من الكاذبين فيما رماها به من الزنا".
ثم تشهد المرأة أربع شهادات تقول في كل مرة: "أشهد بالله إنه لمن الكاذبين فيما رماني به من الزنا، وتقول في الخامسة: "غضب الله عليها إن كان من الصادقين فيما رماني به من الزنا، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه يأتي بلفظ الخطاب، فيقول: "فيما رميتك به من الزنا، وتقول هي: إنك" لمن الكاذبين فيما رميتني به من الزنا"، وفي ظاهر الرواية لا يعتبر الخطاب؛ لأن كلاً منهما يشير للآخر والإشارة أبلغ أسباب التعريف، والخطاب وإن كان أقطع للاحتمال لكن ضمير الغائب إذا اتصل به الإشارة ينقطع الاحتمال أيضاً، وإنما خصت هي بالغضب؛ لأن النساء يستعملن اللعن كثيراً فلا تقع المبالاة به، ويخفن من الغضب، والمراد بالنص نص الشارع يعم والسنة، أي فعل النبي عليه في عويمر العجلاني وامرأته رمز الحقائق: ٢٩٠/١]

باب اللعان
فإن التعنا بانت بتفريق الحاكم، وإن قذف بولد نفى نسبه وألحقه بأمه، وإن أكذب نفسه أي الزوجان المرأة
الزوج بانت بتفريق الحاكم وقال الشافعي: إذا فرغ الزوج من لعانه تقع الفرقة قبل لعالها، ويتعلق بلعانه عنده أربعة أشياء: قطع النسب، وسقوط الحد عنه، ووجوب الحد عليها. وثبوت الفرقة بينهما؛ لأن الزوج لما شهد عليها بالزنا أربع مرات وأكد ذلك باللعان فالظاهر أنهما لا يأتلفان فلم يكن في بقاء النكاح فائدة فينفسخ، ولنا: حديث العجلاني أنه لا عن امرأته فلما فرغا من لعالهما، قال: كذبت عليها يا رسول الله إن أمسكتها، فطلقها ثلاثاً، فلو كانت الفرقة تقع بلعانه لأنكر، بل ورد في رواية أبي داود: فأنفذه عليها، وقال زفر: لا تقع الفرقة إلا إذا تلاعنا جميعاً، فإذا تلاعنا وقعت من غير قضاء؛ لقوله عليه: "المتلاعنان لا يجتمعان أبدا"، رواه أبوداود بمعناه، نفى الاجتماع بينهما بعد التلاعن، فيكون تنصيصاً على وقوع الفرقة بينهما بعد تلاعنهما، وبه قال مالك وأحمد في رواية وعندنا لا تقع إلا بتفريق القاضي بعد التعالهما. ولهذا قال عمر له الله : المتلاعنان يفرق بينهما حتى لو مات أحدهما قبل حكم الحاكم ورثه الآخر؛ لما روي عن ابن عمر ما "أنه عليه لا عن بين رجل وامرأته ففرق بينهما، وألحق الولد بأمه، رواه البخاري ومسلم، ولو وقعت الفرقة لما احتيج إليه، والحديث محمول على بيان حرمة الاستمتاع دون وقوع الحرمة عملاً بهما، ثم التفريق تطليقة بائنة عند الطرفين حتى إذا أكذب نفسه جاز نكاحها وعند أبي :يوسف: تحريم مؤبد، وبه قال الشافعي وزفر ومالك وأحمد واستدلوا بالحديث الذي رواه زفر والجواب عنه أنه إذا أكذب نفسه لم يبق متلاعنا، فلم يتناوله الخبر [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٩٠/١] (فتح) وألحقه بأمه [ أي أم الولد إذا نفي في حالة الولادة. (ط)] لما روينا من حديث البخاري ومسلم، ولأن المقصود نفي الولد فيوفر عليه مقصوده، وإن لم ينف القاضي نسبه صريحاً بل حكم بالتفريق فينتفي نسبه في ضمن الحكم بالتفريق عند الطرفين وعن الثاني أنه لابد للقاضي أن يقول: "ألزمته أمه وأخرجته من الأب" حتى لو لم يقل ذلك لا ينتفي النسب عنه، ثم لا ينتفي من أحكام النسب من جهة الزوج سوى التوارث، وإيجاب النفقة، وأما فيما سوى ذلك مثل رد الشهادة أي شهادة أحدهما للآخر وحرمة النكاح بينهما وحرمة دفع الزكاة، فالنسب قائم إجماعاً، وكيفية هذا اللعان أن يأمر القاضي الرجل فيقول: "أشهد بالله إني لمن الصادقين فيما رميتها به من نفي الولد"، وكذا في جانبها فتقول: "أشهد بالله إنه لمن الكاذبين فيما رماني به من نفي الولد"، ولو قذفها بالزنا ونفى الولد ذكر في اللعان الأمرين كليهما. (مستخلص، عيني) وإن أكذب نفسه [بعد اللعان ولو دلالة بأن مات الولد المنفي عـ مال فادعى نسبه. (ط)] سواء كان الإكذاب باعترافه أو ببينة، أو دلالة يعني لو أكذب نفسه بعد اللعان بأن قال: "كنت كاذبا فيما قلت"، حد حد القذف، وإن أكذب قبل اللعان من عن اللعان، فإن لم يطلقها قبل الإكذاب فكذلك، وإن أبانها ثم أكذب نفسه فلا حد عليه ولا لعان. (مستخلص، فتح)
Book of Divorce. Chapter of Li'an. Ruling: If [the husband] is a valid accuser and she is one whose accuser is not subject to the hadd penalty, then there is no hadd penalty upon him and no li'an. Its description is what the text (al-nass) has stated, i.e. the husband testifies against the wife because it is a substitute for the hadd penalty. The procedure of li'an: hadd penalty because li'an is rendered impossible due to a cause from his side, so one reverts to the original obligation. (ع) Her accuser, if she was an adulteress or a girl or similar. (ط, ع) So no hadd upon him i.e. the husband; because he is truthful in the accusation, but he is given a discretionary punishment (ta'zir). (م, ط,ع) Because of the prohibition, so no hadd upon him and no li'an because she is not eligible for testimony. Thus the impossibility is due to a cause in her, so it does not necessitate the hadd, and li'an is a substitute for it. Similarly if she was insane, or a minor, or had been subjected to hadd for false accusation, then no hadd and no li'an. And if both have been subjected to hadd for false accusation, hadd applies; the slave's li'an is for a cause from his side, as he is not eligible for testimony. Similarly if he and she are both subject to hadd for false accusation, hadd applies. Contrary to if they were both disbelievers or slaves, where the hadd penalty is not obligatory, even if the impossibility is from his side, because accusing a slave woman or a disbelieving woman does not necessitate the hadd penalty. Al-Shafi'i said: Li'an is performed in all cases, except if one of them is a minor or insane or both. He follows his principle that the husband is eligible for the oath, and we follow our principle that he is eligible for testimony. Then ihsan is considered at the time of accusation. So if he accused her while she was a slave or disbelieving, then she embraced Islam or became free, the hadd penalty and li'an are not obligatory. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/290] What the text (al-nass) stated: i.e. what Allah Almighty mentioned in these verses: [Quran 24:6-9]. Know that the reason for revelation of the verse was that Hilal ibn Umayya came to the Messenger of Allah and said: I was absent from my wife for two years, and when I returned I found on her stomach Sharik ibn al-Sahma committing adultery with her. He said to him: 'You must bring four witnesses, otherwise you will be flogged on your back.' Hilal said: 'I saw with my own eyes, O Messenger of Allah,' and repeated this statement, then said: 'I hope that Allah will make a way out for me.' So Allah revealed these verses. This indicates that li'an takes the place of the hadd penalty for slander (qadhf) on the part of the husband, as Hilal was not flogged for his accusation, and it takes the place of the hadd penalty for adultery on the part of the woman; because it is against her. He said at the end of the hadith: 'Were it not for [the] oaths that preceded, I would have had a concern.' So the judge should begin with the husband, and he swears four testimonies, saying each time: 'I testify by Allah that I am among the truthful in what I accused her of regarding adultery,' pointing to her each time, and he says the fifth: 'May the curse of Allah be upon him if he is among the liars in what he accused her of regarding adultery.' Then the woman swears four testimonies, saying each time: 'I testify by Allah that he is among the liars in what he accused me of regarding adultery,' and she says the fifth: 'May the wrath of Allah be upon her if he is among the truthful in what he accused me of regarding adultery.' Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he comes with the address form, saying: 'in what I accused you of regarding adultery,' and she says: 'you are among the liars in what you accused me of regarding adultery.' In the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) the address form is not considered; because each of them points to the other, and pointing is the strongest means of identification. And although the address form is more definitive in removing ambiguity, when the pronoun of the absent person is connected to pointing, it also removes ambiguity. She is specifically mentioned with 'wrath' because women frequently use curses, so they do not pay attention to it, and they fear wrath. The intended meaning of 'al-nass' is the text of the Lawgiver generally, and the Sunnah, i.e. the action of the Prophet concerning 'Uwaymir al-'Ajlani and his wife. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/290] The Book. [PAGE_495] Book of Divorce. 494. Chapter of Li'an. Then if they both performed li'an, she becomes separated by the ruling of the judge. If he accused [her] regarding a child, he denies his lineage and attaches him to his mother. If he retracts his own statement (akdhaba nafsahu) i.e. the husband retracts his accusation of the woman, the husband becomes separated by the ruling of the judge. Al-Shafi'i said: When the husband finishes his li'an, the separation occurs before her li'an. According to him, four things are attached to his li'an: severance of lineage, dropping of the hadd penalty from him, obligation of hadd upon her, and establishment of separation between them. Because when the husband testified against her four times and emphasized that with li'an, it is apparent that they cannot be united, so there is no benefit in the continuation of marriage, so it dissolves. Our evidence: The hadith of al-'Ajlani that he performed li'an with his wife; when they both finished their li'an, he said: 'I would have lied against her, O Messenger of Allah, if I had kept her,' so he divorced her three times. So if separation had occurred by his li'an, he would have denied it. Rather, in the narration of Abu Dawud: 'So he (the Prophet) enforced it upon her.' Zafar said: Separation does not occur unless both have performed li'an together. When they have performed li'an, it occurs without a judicial ruling, because of his statement: 'The two mutala'in (those who perform li'an) are never to be together forever,' narrated by Abu Dawud with its meaning. He negated the union between them after the li'an, so this is a specification that separation occurs between them after their li'an. This is also the view of Malik and Ahmad in one narration. According to us, it does not occur except by the separation of the judge after their li'an. That is why 'Umar said: The two who perform li'an are separated until if one of them dies before the judge's ruling, the other inherits from him. Based on what is narrated from Ibn 'Umar: 'The Prophet performed li'an between a man and his wife, then separated them and attached the child to his mother,' narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. If separation had occurred, it would not have been needed. The hadith is interpreted to indicate the prohibition of enjoyment without the occurrence of prohibition (of remarriage) to act upon both. Then the separation is a final divorce (talaq ba'in) according to both parties (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf or the two shaykhs?). So if he retracts his statement, it becomes permissible for him to marry her. According to Abu Yusuf, it is a permanent prohibition, and this is the view of al-Shafi'i, Zafar, Malik, and Ahmad. They adduced the hadith narrated by Zafar. The answer to it is that when he retracts his statement, he is no longer a mutala'in, so the report does not apply to him. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/290] (Fath) And he attaches him to his mother i.e. the mother of the child if he denies during childbirth. (ط) Based on what we narrated from the hadith of Bukhari and Muslim, and because the intended goal is to deny the child, so his goal is achieved. If the judge did not explicitly deny his lineage but ruled for separation, his lineage is denied implicitly in the ruling for separation according to both parties. According to the second narrator (i.e. Abu Yusuf), it is necessary for the judge to say: 'I have attached him to his mother and removed him from the father,' so if he does not say that, the lineage is not denied from him. Then, from the rulings of lineage on the part of the husband, only inheritance and obligation of maintenance are denied. As for other matters such as rejection of testimony i.e. testimony of one of them for the other, prohibition of marriage between them, and prohibition of giving zakat, the lineage remains by consensus. The procedure of this li'an is that the judge commands the man to say: 'I testify by Allah that I am among the truthful in what I accused her of regarding the denial of the child.' Similarly on her part she says: 'I testify by Allah that he is among the liars in what he accused me of regarding the denial of the child.' If he accused her of adultery and denied the child, both matters are mentioned in the li'an. (Mustakhlas, 'Ayni) If he retracts his statement after the li'an, even by implication, meaning if the denied child dies and inherits property and he claims his lineage, whether the retraction is by his confession or by evidence or by indication, meaning if he retracts after li'an by saying 'I was lying in what I said,' he is subjected to the hadd penalty for slander (hadd al-qadhf). If he retracts before the li'an, from... the li'an. If he did not divorce her before the retraction, it is likewise. If he had separated her (by divorce) then retracts, then no hadd upon him and no li'an. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the chapter of Li'an (mutual imprecation). The author begins with a general ruling: if a husband accuses his wife of adultery but she is someone whose accuser is not subject to the hadd penalty for slander (e.g., a known adulteress, a minor, or an insane woman), then the husband is not to be flogged, nor does he perform li'an. This is because the impossibility of establishing hadd arises from her side, not from his lack of proof. The passage then details the procedure of li'an exactly as specified in the Quran (Surah al-Nur 24:6-9). The reason for revelation concerning Hilal ibn Umayya is given, showing that li'an substitutes for the hadd of slander for the husband and for the hadd of adultery for the wife. The judge begins with the husband, who swears four oaths that he is truthful, and a fifth invoking the curse of Allah upon himself if he is lying. The wife then swears four oaths that he is lying, and a fifth invoking the wrath of Allah upon herself if he is truthful. There is a mention of a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad on behalf of Abu Hanifa allowing direct address, but the relied-upon (zahir al-riwaya) view is that indirect reference with pointing is sufficient. After li'an, the judge separates the couple, and any child born is attributed to the mother only. The passage then addresses a key intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute: when does separation occur? Abu Hanifa and the majority of the Hanafi school hold that separation does not occur until the judge formally separates them after both have completed li'an. Al-Shafi'i, and in one view Zafar, Malik, and Ahmad, hold that separation occurs as soon as the husband finishes his oaths. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of 'Uwaymir al-'Ajlani, who, after li'an, divorced his wife himself, implying that separation had not yet occurred. The hadith 'the two mutala'in are never to be together' is interpreted by the Hanafis as a prohibition of cohabitation, not an automatic divorce. Therefore, if one of them dies before the judge's ruling, the other inherits. Regarding the effect of retraction (ikdhab al-nafs) by the husband: if he admits after li'an that he lied, he is subject to the hadd of slander. If he retracts before li'an, no hadd. The passage also discusses the difference in opinion on whether the separation is a final divorce (talaq ba'in) or a permanent prohibition (tahrim mu'abbad). According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is a ba'in divorce, so if he retracts, he can remarry her. Abu Yusuf, al-Shafi'i, Zafar, Malik, and Ahmad say it is a permanent prohibition. The Hanafi response is that the hadith cited for permanence applies only to the mutala'in, and after retraction he is no longer such.

Key Terms
لعان (li‘ān): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses. It substitutes for the hadd penalty.
قذف (qadhf): Falsely accusing a married person of adultery without witnesses.
إكذاب النفس (ikdhāb an-nafs): The husband's retraction of his accusation after having performed li'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the separation (firqah) occur after the performance of li'an?
A) The moment the husband finishes his final oath.
B) Only after the judge issues a ruling of separation.
C) After both spouses have completed their oaths, automatically without a judge.
D) The marriage is not dissolved by li'an; it remains valid.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, li'an is a wajib procedure that substitutes hadd, and the separation of the spouses requires a judge's ruling after both complete their oaths.

The Hanafi Ruling on Li'an: Separation, Retraction, and Exceptions
Comprehensive treatment of li'an rulings including disputes and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the timing of separation in li'an, the effects of retraction, and the exceptional cases where li'an is not required, and evaluate the related inter- and intra-madhhab disputes.

Core Idea
Li'an does not automatically dissolve marriage; a judge's decree is needed, retraction nullifies the li'an, and certain conditions prevent li'an.

The chapter of li'an (mutual cursing) governs when a husband accuses his wife of adultery or denies paternity. The Hanafi school has detailed rulings on when separation occurs, how retraction affects the marriage, and exceptional cases such as a mute spouse or conditional accusations. This lesson explores these rulings, the proofs from hadith, and the disagreements with other schools and within the Hanafi school itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core Hanafi ruling on separation
State that separation occurs only by the judge's decree after both spouses have performed li'an. Note the requirement of judicial intervention.
2
Examine the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i
Compare Shafi'i's view that separation occurs immediately after the husband's li'an with the Hanafi view. Analyze the hadith of al-'Ajlani used by the Hanafis.
Key proof: the Prophet did not separate the couple until after both finished, and the husband then divorced her himself.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute (Zufar) and the response
Zufar holds that separation occurs automatically after both li'an without a judge. Understand the Hanafi rebuttal distinguishing between prohibition of intimacy and legal dissolution.
The hadith 'the two li'an performers will never be together again' is interpreted as a prohibition, not an automatic divorce.
4
Discuss retraction (akdhaba nafsahu) and its consequences
If the husband retracts his accusation after li'an, he is flogged (hadd) and the marriage becomes dissolved. He may remarry her after hadd, except according to Abu Yusuf who holds a permanent prohibition.
The majority view allows remarriage; Abu Yusuf's view is rejected in the mufta bihi position.
5
Identify special cases where li'an is not applicable
List the exceptions: mute spouse (li'an not required via gestures), denial of pregnancy before birth (conditional accusation not sufficient), and explicit accusation 'zanayti' (li'an obligatory). Note the disputes with Shafi'i and others.
For pregnancy denial, li'an becomes obligatory only after birth within the minimum pregnancy duration.

فإن التعنا بانت بتفريق الحاكم، وإن قذف بولد نفى نسبه وألحقه بأمه، وإن أكذب نفسه أي الزوجان المرأة الزوج بنفي ولد القاضي أي نسب الولد عن الزوج بانت بتفريق الحاكم وقال الشافعي: إذا فرغ الزوج من لعانه تقع الفرقة قبل لعالها، ويتعلق بلعانه عنده أربعة أشياء: قطع النسب، وسقوط الحد عنه، ووجوب الحد عليها. وثبوت الفرقة بينهما؛ لأن الزوج لما شهد عليها بالزنا أربع مرات وأكد ذلك باللعان فالظاهر أنهما لا يأتلفان فلم يكن في بقاء النكاح فائدة فينفسخ، ولنا: حديث العجلاني أنه لا عن امرأته فلما فرغا من لعالهما، قال: كذبت عليها يا رسول الله إن أمسكتها، فطلقها ثلاثاً، فلو كانت الفرقة تقع بلعانه لأنكر ، بل ورد في رواية أبي داود: فأنفذه عليها، وقال زفر: لا تقع الفرقة إلا إذا تلاعنا جميعاً، فإذا تلاعنا وقعت من غير قضاء؛ لقوله عليه: "المتلاعنان لا يجتمعان أبدا"، رواه أبوداود بمعناه، نفى الاجتماع بينهما بعد التلاعن، فيكون تنصيصاً على وقوع الفرقة بينهما بعد تلاعنهما، وبه قال مالك وأحمد في رواية وعندنا لا تقع إلا بتفريق القاضي بعد التعالهما. ولهذا قال عمر له الله : المتلاعنان يفرق بينهما حتى لو مات أحدهما قبل حكم الحاكم ورثه الآخر؛ لما روي عن ابن عمر ما "أنه عليه لا عن بين رجل وامرأته ففرق بينهما، وألحق الولد بأمه، رواه البخاري ومسلم، ولو وقعت الفرقة لما احتيج إليه، والحديث محمول على بيان حرمة الاستمتاع دون وقوع الحرمة عملاً بهما، ثم التفريق تطليقة بائنة عند الطرفين حتى إذا أكذب نفسه جاز نكاحها وعند أبي :يوسف: تحريم مؤبد، وبه قال الشافعي وزفر ومالك وأحمد واستدلوا بالحديث الذي رواه زفر والجواب عنه أنه إذا أكذب نفسه لم يبق متلاعنا، فلم يتناوله الخبر [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٩٠/١] (فتح) وألحقه بأمه [ أي أم الولد إذا نفي في حالة الولادة. (ط)] لما روينا من حديث البخاري ومسلم، ولأن المقصود نفي الولد فيوفر عليه مقصوده، وإن لم ينف القاضي نسبه صريحاً بل حكم بالتفريق فينتفي نسبه في ضمن الحكم بالتفريق عند الطرفين وعن الثاني أنه لابد للقاضي أن يقول: "ألزمته أمه وأخرجته من الأب" حتى لو لم يقل ذلك لا ينتفي النسب عنه، ثم لا ينتفي من أحكام النسب من جهة الزوج سوى التوارث، وإيجاب النفقة، وأما فيما سوى ذلك مثل رد الشهادة أي شهادة أحدهما للآخر وحرمة النكاح بينهما وحرمة دفع الزكاة، فالنسب قائم إجماعاً، وكيفية هذا اللعان أن يأمر القاضي الرجل فيقول: "أشهد بالله إني لمن الصادقين فيما رميتها به من نفي الولد"، وكذا في جانبها فتقول: "أشهد بالله إنه لمن الكاذبين فيما رماني به من نفي الولد"، ولو قذفها بالزنا ونفى الولد ذكر في اللعان الأمرين كليهما. (ط)] سواء كان الإكذاب باعترافه أو ببينة، أو دلالة يعني لو أكذب نفسه بعد اللعان بأن قال: "كنت كاذبا فيما قلت"، حد حد القذف، وإن أكذب قبل اللعان من عن اللعان، فإن لم يطلقها قبل الإكذاب فكذلك، وإن أبانها ثم أكذب نفسه فلا حد عليه ولا لعان. (مستخلص، فتح)
حد، وله أن ينكحها، وكذا إن قذف غيرها فحد أو زنت فحدت، ولا لعان أي للزوج بعد ما أكذب نفسه وحد أي الرجل أي غير امرأته لذلك أي المرأة بقذف الأخرس ونفي الحمل، وتلاعنا بزنيت وهذا الحمل منه، و لم ينف الحمل، ... أي الزوجان نفسه القذف لم يبق الزنا أي القاضي حد حد القذف لإقراره بوجوب الحد عليه. (مستخلص، عيني) وكذا إن قذف أي كذلك يحل له بعد اللعان أن يتزوجها إذا قذف غيرها فحد؛ لأنه لم يبق أ أهلاً للعان فخرج أن يكون متلاعناً، وقوله: "أو زنت فحدت أي كذا يحل له أن يتزوجها إذا زنت المرأة فحدت بالزنا، أو من قذفت إنساناً فحدت؛ لأنها صارت ممن لا يحد قاذفها فخرجت من أهل اللعان، وإنما يتصور هذا إذا تلاعنا بعد التزوج قبل الدخول ثم زنت؛ لأن حدها الجلد حينئذ؛ لأنها ليست بمحصنة، وقوله: "فحدت" وقع اتفاقاً؛ لأن زناها من غير حد يسقط إحصانها ولا لعان إلا بين محصنين بخلاف القذف فإنه لا يسقط به الإحصان حتى يحد،
وضبط بعضهم أو زنت بتشديد النون أي نسب غيرها إلى الزنا وهو القذف فعلى هذا يكون ذكر الحد فيه شرطاً فيزول الإشكال. رمز الحقائق: ۲۹۱/۱] (مستخلص)
ولا لعان بقذف الأخرس أي إذا قذف الأخرس امرأته بالإشارة لا يتعلق به اللعان؛ لأنه يتعلق بالصريح كحد القذف؛ لأن قذفه لا يعرى عن شبهة والحدود تدرأ بها، وكذلك إذا كانت هي خرساء؛ لجواز التصديق لو كانت تنطق فلا يثبت بالشبهة، وقال الشافعي: يجب اللعان به إن كانت له إشارة مفهومة؛ لأن إشارته كالصريح، وبه قال مالك وأحمد. رمز الحقائق: ٢٩١/١] (فتح) ونفي الحمل: أي إذا قال الزوج: ليس حملك مني، فلا لعان أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة وزفر؛ لأن هذا تعليق القذف بالشرط كأنه قال: إن كان بك حمل فهو من الزنا، وذلك ليس بقذف وقالا يجب اللعان إذا جاءت به لأقل ر؛ لأنه تيقن بقيام الحمل منه، فيتحقق القذف، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، وقال الشافعي: يجب اللعان في ستة أشهر؛ من الحال. (عيني، مستخلص)
وتلاعنا بزنيت : أي إذا قال لامرأته زنيت وهذا الحمل من الزنا يجب اللعان؛ لأنه قذفها بصريح الزنا، وقوله: "ولم ينف "الحمل أي لا ينفي القاضي الحمل منه وقال الشافعي: ينفيه؛ لأنه علي نفى ولد هلال وقد قذفها و به قال مالك، ولنا أن الأحكام لا تترتب على الحمل إلا بعد الولادة والحديث محمول على أنه عليه عرف وجود الحمل بطريق الوحي. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٩٢/١] حاملا،
The Book of Divorce. Chapter of Li'an. If they perform li'an, she becomes irrevocably separated by the judge's decree. If he accuses her of adultery regarding a child, he denies its lineage and attaches it to its mother. If he retracts his accusation... (full translation omitted for brevity)
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive treatment of li'an (mutual cursing) in Hanafi fiqh, taken from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins by stating the core ruling: when a husband and wife perform li'an, the marriage is dissolved by an irrevocable divorce (ba'in) through the judge's decree. The text then engages in a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that separation occurs immediately after the husband completes his li'an, before the wife's. The Hanafi position is supported by the hadith of al-'Ajlani where the Prophet did not declare separation until after both had finished li'an. A further dispute with Zufar is noted: he, along with Malik and Ahmad (in one narration), holds that separation occurs automatically after both complete li'an without need for a judge, based on the hadith 'the two li'an performers will never be together again'. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the prohibition of intimacy and actual separation, requiring judicial decree. Additional rulings cover that if one spouse dies before the judge's ruling, inheritance is preserved; the separation is a ba'in divorce allowing remarriage if the husband retracts his accusation, though Abu Yusuf holds it is a permanent prohibition. The text then discusses the procedure of li'an for a mute person (no li'an via gestures, contra Shafi'i), denial of pregnancy (no li'an according to Abu Hanifa and Zufar unless the child is born within minimum pregnancy duration, while Shaybani and others hold it is required), and the specific phrasing 'zanayti' (you committed adultery) which necessitates li'an due to explicit accusation. The passage concludes that the judge does not deny lineage to the husband based on pregnancy alone, as legal effects attach only after birth. Throughout, the commentary cites sources like al-Hidayah, al-‘Inayah, and Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li‘an): Mutual cursing between spouses when husband accuses wife of adultery or denies paternity, involving specific oaths and imprecations.
تفريق الحاكم (tafriq al-hakim): The judicial decree of separation that dissolves the marriage irrevocably (ba'in).
أكذب نفسه (akdhaba nafsahu): The husband's retraction of his accusation after li'an, admitting he lied.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school in this lesson, when does separation occur in li'an?
A) Immediately after the husband completes his li'an
B) After both spouses complete li'an, automatically
C) Only after the judge issues a decree of separation
D) After the wife completes her li'an

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, li'an does not automatically dissolve the marriage; separation requires a judicial decree, preserving inheritance rights until that decree.

Remarriage After Qadhf Retraction and Flogging
Ruling on husband remarrying wife after retracting qadhf and flogging

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the majority of Hanafi scholars permit remarriage after a husband retracts qadhf and is flogged, and evaluate Abu Yusuf's dissenting argument.

Core Idea
After retraction and flogging, the husband regains legal eligibility to marry his ex-wife.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether a husband who falsely accused his wife of zina and then retracted, being flogged, may remarry her. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rule that it is permissible, drawing an analogy with the munafiq who becomes Muslim. Abu Yusuf holds it is permanently forbidden, relying on a hadith. We will follow the reasoning and see how the Hanafi school determines the operative position.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the majority position
Identify the core question: may a husband remarry his wife after retracting a qadhf accusation and being flogged? The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say yes.
2
Identify the majority's proof
The majority uses qiyas (analogy) with the munafiq: just as the prohibition on praying for the munafiq lifts when he becomes Muslim, the prohibition on marriage lifts when the man is no longer eligible for li'an (due to flogging making him fit for testimony).
The Quranic verse 9:84 is cited as supporting the conditionality of the prohibition.
3
Identify the opposing proof
Abu Yusuf cites a hadith from Zufar that indicates permanent prohibition. This is a textual evidence (dalil naqli).
The hadith is not quoted in the passage but referenced.
4
Analyze why the majority's proof outweighs
The majority's analogy is based on a clear principle: prohibitions are contingent on the continuing existence of the cause. Once the cause (being eligible for li'an) is removed, the prohibition lifts. The hadith of Zufar is interpreted as applying only as long as the condition persists.
The Hanafi school often uses istihsan and qiyas to interpret hadith when the literal meaning conflicts with other principles.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the majority, the couple can remarry; under Abu Yusuf, they are permanently separated. The mufta bihi (operative view) is the majority view.
This difference affects actual fatwa in cases of separation after li'an.

Source Text

حد، وله أن ينكحها، وكذا إن قذف غيرها فحد أو زنت فحدت، ولا لعان أي للزوج بعد ما أكذب نفسه وحد أي الرجل أي غير امرأته لذلك أي المرأة بقذف الأخرس ونفي الحمل، وتلاعنا بزنيت وهذا الحمل منه، و لم ينف الحمل، ... أي الزوجان نفسه القذف لم يبق الزنا أي القاضي حد حد القذف لإقراره بوجوب الحد عليه. (ط، ع) وله أن ينكحها أي حل للزوج أن يتزوجها بعد ما أكذب وحد عند الطرفين، وقال أبو يوسف: لا يجوز له التزوج بها أبداً؛ لحديث زفر المذكور، ولهما: أنه لما حد في أهلاً للشهادة فلم يبق أهلاً للعان فلم يكن متلاعناً، ألا ترى أن المنافق إذا أسلم تحل عليه الصلاة. وأنزلت في المنافقين قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تُصَلِّ عَلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْهُمْ مَاتَ أَبدا (التوبة: ٨٤) أي ما دام منافقا، فكذا قوله: المتلاعنان إلخ، أي ما داما على صفة اللعان. (مستخلص، عيني) وكذا إن قذف أي كذلك يحل له بعد اللعان أن يتزوجها إذا قذف غيرها فحد؛ لأنه لم يبق أ أهلاً للعان فخرج أن يكون متلاعناً، وقوله: "أو زنت فحدت أي كذا يحل له أن يتزوجها إذا زنت المرأة فحدت بالزنا، أو من قذفت إنساناً فحدت؛ لأنها صارت ممن لا يحد قاذفها فخرجت من أهل اللعان، وإنما يتصور هذا إذا تلاعنا بعد التزوج قبل الدخول ثم زنت؛ لأن حدها الجلد حينئذ؛ لأنها ليست بمحصنة، وقوله: "فحدت" وقع اتفاقاً؛ لأن زناها من غير حد يسقط إحصانها ولا لعان إلا بين محصنين بخلاف القذف فإنه لا يسقط به الإحصان حتى يحد، وضبط بعضهم أو زنت بتشديد النون أي نسب غيرها إلى الزنا وهو القذف فعلى هذا يكون ذكر الحد فيه شرطاً فيزول الإشكال. رمز الحقائق: ۲۹۱/۱] (مستخلص)
He is flogged, and he may marry her. Likewise if he accused another and was flogged, or she committed zina and was flogged. And no li'an for the husband after he retracts himself and is flogged—meaning the man (other than his wife) for that (the woman) by the qadhf of the mute and negation of pregnancy, and they curse each other with 'you committed zina and this pregnancy is from that' and he did not negate the pregnancy... etc. (then commentary) He may marry her: it is permissible for the husband to marry her after he retracts and is flogged according to both parties. Abu Yusuf said: He may never marry her, due to the hadith of Zufar mentioned. And for them (the two companions): When he is flogged he becomes qualified for testimony, so he no longer qualifies for li'an, thus he is not one who performs li'an. Do you not see that when a munafiq becomes Muslim, prayer is permissible for him, and Allah revealed concerning the munafiqin: 'And never pray for any of them who dies' (9:84) meaning as long as he is a munafiq. Similarly, his statement 'the two li'an parties' etc. means as long as they remain in the condition for li'an. Likewise if he accused: Similarly, it is permissible for him after li'an to marry her if he accused another and was flogged, because he is no longer qualified for li'an and thus ceases to be a mu'tali' (one who performs li'an). And his statement 'or she committed zina and was flogged': Similarly, it is permissible for him to marry her if the woman committed zina and was flogged for zina, or if she accused someone and was flogged, because she became one whose accuser is not flogged, so she leaves the category of those eligible for li'an. This scenario occurs if they performed li'an after marriage before consummation, then she committed zina, because her penalty is flogging at that time since she is not muhsan. His statement 'and she was flogged' occurred coincidentally, because her zina without flogging removes her ihsan, and li'an is only between muhsan individuals, unlike qadhf which does not remove ihsan until he is flogged. Some scholars interpreted 'or she committed zina' with shaddah on the nun, meaning she attributed zina to another, i.e., qadhf, thus mentioning the flogging is a condition and the difficulty is removed. Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/291] (Mukhtasar).
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling from the matn: after a husband retracts his qadhf against his wife and is flogged, he may marry her (or remarry her if divorced). The commentator explains that according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, with Abu Yusuf dissenting), the flogging makes the man qualified for testimony and thus no longer eligible for li'an, so the prohibition disappears. Abu Yusuf argues that the hadith of Zufar indicates permanent prohibition. The commentary also extends the ruling to cases where the husband accused a different woman and was flogged, or where the wife was flogged for zina or for accusing someone—in all cases, the man may marry her because the woman ceases to be subject to li'an. The passage also clarifies that the flogging of the woman for zina removes her ihsan (chastity) only if she was not previously muhsan, and li'an is only between muhsan individuals. The final note explains a variant reading to resolve an inconsistency.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li'ān): Mutual cursing between spouses when the husband accuses his wife of zina but lacks proof, or disclaims paternity, involving specific oaths and imprecations.
القذف (al-qadhf): False accusation of zina against a muhsan person, subjecting the accuser to hadd punishment unless he produces four witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the ruling on a husband who retracts a false accusation (qadhf) against his wife and is flogged?
A) He may never marry her again.
B) He may marry her again after retraction and flogging.
C) He must marry her again but with a new mahr.
D) The marriage is automatically annulled.

Key Takeaway
After a husband retracts a false accusation of zina against his wife and is flogged, he may remarry her according to the Hanafi majority.

No Li'an for Qadhf by a Mute
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the Hanafi school denies li'an for a mute's qadhf and apply the maxim 'al-ḥudūd tudraʾu bial-shubuhāt' to this case.

Core Idea
Li'an requires explicit verbal qadhf; a mute's gesture is ambiguous, so no li'an.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from Kanz al-Daqāʾiq: the case of a mute person who accuses his spouse of zina through gestures. Does this trigger li'an (mutual imprecation)? The Hanafi school, adhering to the maxim that legal penalties are repelled by ambiguities, holds that it does not. We will explore the reasoning behind this position and compare it with the view of other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a mute person's qadhf (false accusation of zina) through gesture. The ruling: li'an is not established (lā liʿān).
Li'an is a specific legal procedure involving mutual oaths; it is tied to the ḥadd of qadhf.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The Hanafi proof is the maxim 'al-ḥudūd tudraʾu bial-shubuhāt' (penalties are repelled by doubts). The mute's gesture is not entirely clear, so it contains shubha.
The ḥadd of qadhf itself would also be repelled by the same doubt.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah (how the proof applies)
Since li'an is linked to the ḥadd of qadhf (both are penalties), the same principle applies: if the qadhf itself is not established due to ambiguity, then li'an cannot follow.
The text also notes the same ruling if the wife is mute, because the possibility of her confirmation (if she could speak) introduces further ambiguity.
4
Note the ikhtilāf (scholarly disagreement)
Imam al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that an understandable gesture is like explicit speech, so li'an is required.
Their evidence: the gesture communicates the same meaning, and the purpose of li'an is to resolve the accusation.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjīḥ (preferred view)
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon view (muftā bihi) in the school, based on the principle of avoiding penalties in cases of doubt.
No intra-Hanafi dispute is recorded on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا لعان بقذف الأخرس أي إذا قذف الأخرس امرأته بالإشارة لا يتعلق به اللعان؛ لأنه يتعلق بالصريح كحد القذف؛ لأن قذفه لا يعرى عن شبهة والحدود تدرأ بها، وكذلك إذا كانت هي خرساء؛ لجواز التصديق لو كانت تنطق فلا يثبت بالشبهة، وقال الشافعي: يجب اللعان به إن كانت له إشارة مفهومة؛ لأن إشارته كالصريح، وبه قال مالك وأحمد. رمز الحقائق: ٢٩١/١] (فتح)
And no li'an by the qadhf of the mute: That is, if a mute person accuses his wife by gesture, li'an is not established thereby, because li'an is attached to explicit speech like the hadd for qadhf, because his qadhf is not free from ambiguity and legal penalties are repelled by ambiguities. Similarly, if the wife is mute, due to the possibility of confirming [the accusation] if she could speak, so [li'an] is not established due to ambiguity. Al-Shafi'i said: Li'an is obligatory by it if he has an understandable gesture, because his gesture is like explicit speech. Malik and Ahmad also said this. Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/291] (Fath).

Commentary
This passage is the expansion of the ruling 'No li'an by qadhf of a mute.' The commentator explains that li'an requires explicit verbal accusation (ṣarīḥ). A mute's gesture involves uncertainty (shubha), and legal penalties (ḥudūd) are repelled by such uncertainties. The same applies if the wife is mute. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that an understandable gesture suffices, equating it with explicit speech, and Malik and Ahmad agree. The Hanafi position relies on the principle of repelling penalties due to ambiguity.

Key Terms
الأخرس (al-akhras): A person who cannot speak (mute), whose communication is through gestures.
الحدود تدرأ بالشبهات (al-ḥudūd tudraʾu bial-shubuhāt): Legal penalties are repelled by ambiguities; a foundational legal maxim used here to negate li'an.
اللعان (al-liʿān): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses the wife of zina without witnesses; involves specific oaths.
القذف (al-qadhf): False accusation of zina; a crime punishable by hadd (80 lashes).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is li'an established if a mute husband accuses his wife of zina by an unmistakable gesture?
A) Yes, because the gesture is as clear as speech.
B) Yes, if the wife understands the gesture.
C) No, because li'an requires explicit verbal speech and the gesture involves ambiguity.
D) No, because mute persons are not eligible for li'an at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school denies li'an for a mute's qadhf by gesture due to the principle that penalties are repelled by ambiguities, a position that differs from the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools.

Negation of Pregnancy: When Does a Husband's Denial Trigger Li'an?
Ruling on conditional denial of paternity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between explicit qadhf and conditional negation of paternity and apply the Hanafi rule that li'an is not required for conditional statements according to Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Denying pregnancy is conditional qadhf, not explicit—no li'an without direct accusation.

This passage examines a nuanced scenario in family law: a husband tells his pregnant wife, "This pregnancy is not from me." Is this an accusation of zina that triggers li'an (mutual cursing) or merely a conditional statement that falls short? The Hanafi school divides internally, and other schools differ. Understanding this distinction is crucial for protecting marriages from hasty separations based on ambiguous remarks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the husband's statement is an act of negating pregnancy. The central question is whether this triggers the obligation of li'an.
Li'an is a procedure where spouses swear oaths to resolve accusations of zina.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa classifies the statement as conditional qadhf (ta'liq al-qadhf). He likens it to saying, 'If you are pregnant, it is from zina,' which is not an explicit accusation.
The implicit condition prevents the statement from being an outright charge.
3
Compare the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require li'an if the wife gives birth before a minimum period (commonly six months). For them, the timing proves the husband must be the father, so his denial becomes a de facto accusation.
The Sahibayn add a temporal criterion: birth within a certain window.
4
Note cross-madhhab views
Malik and Ahmad agree with the Sahibayn. Al-Shafi'i also requires li'an but within a specific period (six months from the statement).
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf across schools.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, no li'an is needed, and the marriage continues. Under the opposing view, li'an becomes obligatory, which can lead to permanent separation.
The practical consequence affects the stability of the marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونفي الحمل: أي إذا قال الزوج: ليس حملك مني، فلا لعان أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة وزفر؛ لأن هذا تعليق القذف بالشرط كأنه قال: إن كان بك حمل فهو من الزنا، وذلك ليس بقذف وقالا يجب اللعان إذا جاءت به لأقل ر؛ لأنه تيقن بقيام الحمل منه، فيتحقق القذف، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، وقال الشافعي: يجب اللعان في ستة أشهر؛ من الحال. (عيني، مستخلص)
And negation of pregnancy: That is, if the husband says 'This pregnancy is not from me,' there is no li'an according to Abu Hanifa and Zufar, because this is a conditional qadhf, as if he said 'If there is a pregnancy in you, it is from zina,' and that is not [explicit] qadhf. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Li'an is obligatory if she brings the child before six months? Because it is certain that the pregnancy is established from him, so qadhf is realized. Malik and Ahmad said the same. Al-Shafi'i said: Li'an is obligatory within six months? from the situation. (Ayni, Mukhtasar).
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on a husband who says to his pregnant wife 'This pregnancy is not from me.' According to Abu Hanifa and Zufar, this is not an explicit accusation of zina but a conditional statement, so no li'an is required. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions) hold that if the wife gives birth before a certain minimum period (likely six months), the husband's negation is a de facto qadhf because the pregnancy must be from him, thus li'an is required. Malik and Ahmad agree with the two companions. Imam al-Shafi'i also requires li'an but within six months. The Hanafi majority position (Abu Hanifa and Zufar) is that li'an is not triggered by such a conditional statement.

Key Terms
نفي الحمل (nafy al-ḥaml): A husband's declaration that his pregnant wife's fetus is not from him.
القذف المعلق (al-qadhf al-mu'allaq): Conditional accusation of zina, e.g., 'If you are pregnant, it is from zina.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Li'an is required immediately.
B) Li'an is required only if the child is born.
C) Li'an is not required because the statement is conditional.
D) Li'an is required if the wife admits zina.

Key Takeaway
A husband's conditional denial of pregnancy does not constitute explicit qadhf, so li'an is not required according to Abu Hanifa and Zufar.

Explicit Accusation of Zina and Pregnancy Requires Li'an
Ruling when husband explicitly accuses wife of zina and pregnancy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on li'an when a husband explicitly accuses his wife of zina and explain why the judge does not negate the child's paternity during pregnancy.

Core Idea
Li'an is wajib upon explicit zina accusation; paternity negation only after birth, not during pregnancy.

This passage clarifies the Hanafi position when a husband explicitly says 'You committed zina and this pregnancy is from that zina.' The key distinction is between explicit accusation (ṣarīḥ al-zinā) triggering li'an and the timing of paternity negation. The judge does not automatically negate the child's lineage from the husband during pregnancy, contrary to the Shafi'i and Maliki schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What exactly did the husband say? The text states he said 'you committed zina' explicitly. The ruling is that li'an is wajib because it is an explicit accusation (qadhf).
The mention of pregnancy does not change the obligation; it is part of the accusation.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi position relies on the general principle that legal rulings regarding pregnancy (like paternity) are only established after birth. Therefore, the judge cannot negate the child during pregnancy.
This is a rule of fiqh: al-ahkām lā tatabattatu ʿalā al-ḥaml illā baʿda al-wilādah.
3
State the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that the judge should negate the child's paternity immediately, based on the precedent of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib in the case of Hilal. The Prophet ﷺ had 'Ali make the judgment, and he negated the child.
This is recorded in the Hadith of Hilal.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi scholars respond that the Hadith of Hilal is specific to that case because the Prophet ﷺ knew of the pregnancy through revelation. Hence, it does not establish a general rule. The general rule remains that paternity cannot be negated before birth.
This is an example of takhṣīṣ (specification) of a general principle by a specific evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And his statement 'and he did not negate the pregnancy' means the judge does not negate the pregnancy from him. Al-Shafi'i said: He negates it, because 'Ali negated the child of Hilal after he accused her, and Malik also said this. Our proof: Legal rulings regarding pregnancy are only established after birth, and the hadith is interpreted to mean that the Prophet ﷺ knew of the pregnancy through revelation. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/292] pregnant?
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where a husband explicitly says to his wife 'You committed zina and this pregnancy is from that zina.' The commentator states that li'an is obligatory because this is a clear accusation (ṣarīḥ al-qadhf). The husband's statement does not include a negation of the pregnancy; rather, it attributes it to zina. The judge does not automatically negate the child's lineage from the husband. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the judge should negate the child's paternity, citing the precedent of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib in the case of Hilal. The Hanafi response is that rulings on pregnancy apply only after birth, and the hadith is understood to refer to a special case where the Prophet knew through divine revelation.

Key Terms
صريح الزنا (ṣarīḥ al-zinā): Explicit verbal accusation of having committed zina.
نفي الولد (nafy al-walad): Negation of a child's paternity by the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The child's paternity is automatically negated.
D) The husband must be flogged for qadhf.

Key Takeaway
Explicit accusation of zina makes li'an obligatory; paternity negation is only after birth, not during pregnancy.

Timing of Paternity Negation: At Congratulation or Purchase of Birthing Tools
Ruling on validity of paternity negation at specific times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when paternity negation is valid and apply the principle of custom ('urf) to determine the permissible period.

Core Idea
Negation of paternity is only valid promptly after birth; custom defines 'promptly'.

In Hanafi fiqh, a husband who wishes to negate the paternity of his wife's newborn must do so immediately upon learning of the birth. The classical texts mention the time of congratulation or purchase of birthing tools as indicators. This lesson unpacks the ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams and the relied-upon view that custom determines the period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act is the husband's negation of the child's lineage (نفي الولد). The default ruling is that it is valid only if done at the time of congratulation (التهنئة) or when purchasing birthing tools (ابتاع آلة الولادة). After that period, it is invalid and the child is firmly attributed to him.
The ruling applies only if the child is alive at the time of negation.
2
Understand the underlying rationale
The reason is that silence after the appropriate time indicates acceptance (التزام). The principle 'تقادم العهد دليل الالتزام' is invoked. Thus, delaying negation beyond the customary period forfeits the right.
This is a rational (aqli) proof based on customary inference.
3
Explore the Hanafi intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on duration
Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to have said 7 days or 3 days; the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said the period of nifas (up to 40 days). The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that it is not fixed but determined by custom ('urf).
The report from Hasan ibn Ziyad is nawadir but the tarjih is based on the principle that setting specific numbers by opinion is invalid.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i has two opinions: immediate (fawran) or within three days. The Hanafi view differs by allowing a bit more leeway based on custom, not a strict number.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in a Hanafi context, a negation after a few days may be valid if custom considers it prompt.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling to a scenario
If a husband returns from a journey 20 days after birth and immediately negates, it is invalid because custom does not consider 20 days prompt. The child remains his. If he negates upon receiving congratulations on the same day, it is valid.
Custom is assessed locally; a short period (a few days) is acceptable, a month or more is not.

(Full translation would be very long; summarizing key parts:) And if he negates the child at the time of congratulation or purchase of birthing tools, it is valid, and after that not valid, and li'an occurs in both. And if the husband negates the first of twins and acknowledges the second, he is flogged; if the reverse, li'an occurs; and the lineage of both is established in both cases... (commentary on congratulation, purchase, timing, ikhtilaf).
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage covers two independent rulings. First: A husband's negation of paternity is valid only if done at the time of congratulation (when people congratulate him on the birth) or when purchasing birthing tools (like a cradle). After that period, the negation is invalid due to the presumption of acceptance over time. There is ikhtilaf on the exact duration: Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to have said 7 days or 3 days; the two companions say the period of lochia (nifas); Shafi'i has two opinions. The relied-upon view is that it is determined by custom ('urf): a short period is acceptable, a long one is not. Second: The twins case: If a woman gives birth to twins and the husband negates the first but acknowledges the second, he is flogged for qadhf because acknowledging the second disproves the negation of the first (since both come from one act of conception). If he acknowledges the first and negates the second, he must perform li'an, and the lineage of both is established. The text also discusses if both are negated and one dies before li'an.

Key Terms
التهنئة (al-tahni'a): The congratulation given at the birth of a child, e.g., 'May Allah gladden your eyes.'
النفاس (al-nifās): Postpartum bleeding; the period during which a woman is considered in a state of nifas, up to 40 days according to Hanafi fiqh.
الالتزام (al-iltizām): Acceptance or consent inferred from behavior, especially silence after a customary period.

Key Takeaway
Paternity negation is valid only within a customary short period after birth; the relied-upon Hanafi view does not fix a specific number but refers to custom.

Paternity of Twins: Negation and Acknowledgment
Ruling on twin paternity for negation and acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on twin paternity cases: when negation of one twin triggers a legal consequence for both.

Core Idea
Twins are from one conception; negating one affects the other, and inconsistency leads to punishment or li'an.

When a woman gives birth to twins, the husband's treatment of them in terms of acknowledgment or negation has a specific legal logic. Because twins are created from a single act of conception, they are legally inseparable in lineage. This lesson explains the four scenarios: negating the first and acknowledging the second, the reverse, negating both, and the effect of one twin's death before li'an.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
The principle is that twins are created from one water (ماء واحد). Therefore, their lineages are necessarily the same. Acknowledging one implies acknowledging the other, and negating one implies negating the other. Inconsistency (negating one and acknowledging the other) is tantamount to self-contradiction.
2
First scenario: Negate first, acknowledge second
If the husband negates the first twin (says it is not his) but acknowledges the second, he is flogged (حد القذف). Reason: by acknowledging the second, he admits that the wife had sexual intercourse with him at the relevant time, so the negation of the first is a false accusation of adultery against his wife.
Flogging is for slander (qadhf), not for theft or zina.
3
Second scenario: Acknowledge first, negate second
If he acknowledges the first but negates the second, he must perform li'an (mutual cursing). Reason: he first affirmed the wife's fidelity (by acknowledging the first), then accused her of adultery (by negating the second). Li'an is required to resolve the contradiction.
Li'an is a special oath-taking process; if he refuses, he is flogged.
4
Lineage outcome in both scenarios
In both scenarios, the lineage of both twins is established as his. Because the negation is either self-contradictory (first scenario) or overridden by prior acknowledgment (second scenario). The rule: 'Nafi after acknowledgment is not considered, but acknowledgment after negation is considered.'
5
Third scenario: Negate both twins; one dies before li'an
If he negates both, he must perform li'an for each. If one twin dies before the li'an, according to Imam Muhammad, the li'an must still be performed between the spouses regarding the deceased twin, because the accusation remains. The living twin's li'an is also required.
Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf may differ? The text only mentions Muhammad's view.

(ع)] أي فيما إذا صح نفيه أو فيما إذا لم يصح ولم ينف النسب فيما إذا نفى بعد الوقت المذكور، وإنما وجب اللعان لوجود القذف صريحاً بنفي الولد البحر الرائق: ۱۸۸/۱] (مستخلص) التوأمين: التوأم "فوعل والأنثى توأمة والاثنان توأمان وهما اللذان بين ولادتيهما أقل. ستة أشهر". (مصباح وزيلعي) وأقر بالثاني: أي إذا ولدت المرأة ولدين في بطن واحد، ونفى الزوج أولهما واعترف بالثاني، حد الزوج للقذف؛ لأنه لما أقر بالثاني فقد أكذب نفسه في نفي الأول؛ لأنهما خلقا من ماء واحد (مستخلص) حد: لأنه أكذب نفسه بدعوى الثاني. (ع) من وإن عكس لاعن: أي وإن أقر بالأول ثم نفى الثاني يجب اللعان؛ لأنه اعترف أولاً بعفتها ثم قذفها بالزنا فيجب اللعان، وقوله: "وثبت نسبهما فيهما" أي يثبت نسب الولدين في الصورتين جميعاً، فثبوت نسب أحدهما يلزم ثبوت نسب الآخر ونفي أحدهما استلزم نفي الآخر إلا أن النفي بعد الإقرار غير معتبر والإقرار بعد النفي يعتبر، ولو نفاهما ثم مات أحدهما قبل اللعان لزماه ويلا عن بينهما عند محمد لوجود القذف. (عيني، مستخلص) فيهما: أي في المسألتين جميعاً؛ لأنهما خلقا . من ماء واحد. (ط)
(Full translation would be very long; summarizing key parts:) And if he negates the child at the time of congratulation or purchase of birthing tools, it is valid, and after that not valid, and li'an occurs in both. And if the husband negates the first of twins and acknowledges the second, he is flogged; if the reverse, li'an occurs; and the lineage of both is established in both cases... (commentary on congratulation, purchase, timing, ikhtilaf).
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage covers two independent rulings. First: A husband's negation of paternity is valid only if done at the time of congratulation (when people congratulate him on the birth) or when purchasing birthing tools (like a cradle). After that period, the negation is invalid due to the presumption of acceptance over time. There is ikhtilaf on the exact duration: Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to have said 7 days or 3 days; the two companions say the period of lochia (nifas); Shafi'i has two opinions. The relied-upon view is that it is determined by custom ('urf): a short period is acceptable, a long one is not. Second: The twins case: If a woman gives birth to twins and the husband negates the first but acknowledges the second, he is flogged for qadhf because acknowledging the second disproves the negation of the first (since both come from one act of conception). If he acknowledges the first and negates the second, he must perform li'an, and the lineage of both is established. The text also discusses if both are negated and one dies before li'an.

Key Terms
توأم (taw'am): Twin; two children born from one pregnancy, with less than six months between births.
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): Punishment for false accusation of adultery: 80 lashes for a free person.
لاعن (lā'an): He performed li'an (mutual cursing oath) between spouses to resolve an accusation of adultery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband acknowledges the first twin but negates the second. What is the ruling?
A) He is flogged for slander.
B) He must perform li'an.
C) The second twin is not his.
D) No consequence.

Key Takeaway
Twins are legally one unit; inconsistent acknowledgment/negation leads to flogging or li'an, and lineage of both is established unless properly negated via li'an.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
The One-Year Deferral and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Separation
Ruling on impotent husband with deferral and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the impotent husband, distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether a judge's decree is required for separation, and apply the rule to resolve a case where the husband refuses to divorce.

Core Idea
Impotence gives the wife a right to separation after one year — but does she need a judge's decree or is it automatic?

This lesson tackles a sensitive family matter: what happens when a husband cannot consummate the marriage? The Hanafi school provides a clear mechanism — a one-year deferral established by the consensus of the Companions. However, within the school, there is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, concerning the process of separation: does the wife automatically become separated after the year, or must the judge decree the separation if the husband refuses to divorce? Understanding this difference is crucial for the practicing mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the deferral period
The passage addresses the impotent husband (al-‘innin), including eunuchs. The key is the one-year deferral (ta’jeel) from the date of the wife's complaint. If the husband has intercourse even once within that year, the deferral is void and the wife loses her right to separation on that ground.
The one-year period is based on the consensus of the Companions, as cited in the text.
2
Determine the condition for separation
If the husband does not consummate within the year, the wife may seek separation. The condition is that she must request it (or her agent if she is absent). If she is a slave, the master makes the request. The separation is a single irrevocable divorce (talaq bain).
The wife's request is required; the husband's consent is not needed.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the mechanism
Abu Hanifa holds that separation requires the judge's decree (tafriq) if the husband refuses to divorce. The judge stands in the husband's place to effect the divorce. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that separation occurs automatically after the year, because the law gave her the choice at that point, without needing a judge.
The disagreement is about who initiates the termination: the judge or automatic law.
4
Apply the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa: the wife must obtain a judge's decree. This is the operative ruling for fatwa today. The Sahibayn's view is considered a narration (riwaya) from Abu Hanifa and not the primary position.
The commentary (Fath / ‘Ayni) presents Abu Hanifa's view as the primary and the Sahibayn's as a narration.
5
Identify the proof for the deferral
The one-year deferral is established by the consensus (ijma) of the Companions. The text also refutes a hadith from Abd al-Rahman, stating it was after divorce and thus not a proof for a different position.
The proof is dalil naqli (transmitted evidence) from ijma, not from a specific hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق
باب العنين
فإن وطئ وإلا بانت بالتفريق إن طلبت فلو قال: "وطئت" وأنكرت، وقلن
المرأة
"بكر" خيرت، وإن كانت ثيباً صدق بحلفه،
بأن قلن هي ثيب أي الزوج أي بيمينه
أي وطئتها في السنة أي المرأة الوطء
عدم تحريك آلته، ولنا: إجماع الصحابة له على تأجيله وقال ابن البر : قد صح أن حديث عبد الرحمن كان بعد طلاقها فلا يكون حجة [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٩٣/١] (فتح)
فإن وطئ ولو مرة واحدة في السنة فيها وبطل التأجيل (ط)] أي العنين أو الخصي في السنة، جواب الشرط محذوف أي فبها ونعمت ثم بالوطء ولو مرة واحدة يبطل التأجيل؛ لاستيفائها حقها مرة، وما زاد فهو مستحق عليه ديانة، ولهذا يأثم إذا تركها متعنتاً مع القدرة عليه. (فتح)
وإلا بانت [ أي وإن لم يطأها العنين أو الخصي لاستمرار عجزه. (ع)] أي وإن لم يطأها في السنة بانت المرأة بتفريق القاضي عند امتناع الزوج عن تطليقها وهذا عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه لما تعذر عليه الإمساك بالمعروف وجب عليه التسريح بالإحسان، فإن فعل الزوج وطلق فيها، وإلا ناب القاضي منابه دفعاً للظلم عنها، وعندهما وهو رواية عنه: بانت بغير تفريق؛ لأن الشرع خيرها عند تمام الحول، وقوله: "إن طلبت" راجع إلى الكل أي التفريق والتأجيل والبينونة وطلب وكيلها بالتفريق عند غيبتها كطلبها، ثم الفرقة طلقة بائنة عندنا، وعند الشافعي وأحمد هي فسخ؛ لأنه فرقة من جهتها، ولنا أن هذه الفرقة من جهته؛ لأن الواجب عليه الإمساك، فإذا فات وجب التسريح، فلما امتنع . هو قام القاضي مقامه، فكان الفعل منسوباً إليه فكان طلاقاً بائناً ليتحقق دفع الظلم عنها، والنكاح الصحيح النافذ اللازم لا يحتمل الفسخ. (عيني، فتح) بالتفريق أي بتفريق الزوج والحاكم. (ع) إن طلبت المرأة التفريق؛ لأن ذلك حقها، وهذا إذا كانت حرة، ولو أمة فالطلب لسيدها. (ط)
The Book of Divorce. Chapter of the Impotent Husband. If he has intercourse, otherwise she is separated by the separation if she requests. If he says, 'I have had intercourse' and she denies, and the women say 'virgin', she is given choice, and if she is non-virgin, he is believed with his oath. Because if they say she is non-virgin, meaning the husband, meaning by his oath, meaning I have had intercourse with her in the year, meaning the woman's intercourse. The lack of movement of his organ. And for us: consensus of the Companions for his deferment. Ibn al-Barr said: The hadith of Abd al-Rahman was after her divorce, so it is not a proof. If he has intercourse even once in the year, it is valid and the deferment becomes void. Meaning the impotent or the eunuch in the year, the answer of the condition is omitted, meaning it is good. Then by intercourse even once, the deferment becomes void because she has received her right once, and what is more is incumbent upon him in the religious sense, and therefore he sins if he leaves her intentionally with ability. Otherwise she separates: meaning if the impotent or eunuch does not have intercourse with her due to the continuance of his inability, meaning if he does not have intercourse with her in the year, the woman separates by the separation of the judge when the husband refuses to divorce her, and this according to Abu Hanifa; because when he is unable to retain with kindness, it is obligatory to release with goodness. If the husband does so and divorces her, otherwise the judge takes his place to prevent oppression from her. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and it is a narration from him: she separates without separation because the law gave her choice at the completion of the year. His statement 'if she requests' refers to all, meaning separation, deferment, and final separation. The request of her agent for separation in her absence is like her request. Then the separation is a irrevocable divorce according to us, while according to al-Shafi'i and Ahmad it is annulment because it is a separation from her side. And for us: this separation is from his side because the obligation on him is retention, so when it fails, release is obligatory. So when he refrained, the judge took his place, so the act is attributed to him, so it is an irrevocable divorce to realize the removal of oppression from her. The valid, effective, and binding marriage does not admit annulment. By separation: meaning by separation of the husband and the ruler. If the woman requests separation because it is her right, and this if she is free; if she is a slave, then the request belongs to her master.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the impotent husband combined with an intra-Hanafi dispute. It begins with the main ruling: if an impotent husband (or eunuch) has intercourse within one year, the deferral period ends; if he does not, the wife is separated by the judge's decree if she requests. The commentary explains that the one-year period is established by the consensus of the Companions. If the husband consummates even once, her right to separation is fulfilled; additional intercourse is religiously incumbent but not legally required. Then the intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: Abu Hanifa holds that separation requires the judge's decree (tafriq) when the husband refuses to divorce. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions) hold that separation occurs automatically after one year without the judge, because the law gave her the choice at that point. The phrase 'if she requests' is interpreted by Abu Hanifa to apply to all aspects: deferral, separation, and finality. The passage also addresses the inter-madhhab difference: according to Hanafis, the separation is an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain), while Shafi'i and Ahmad consider it an annulment (faskh). The Hanafi proof is that the marriage is valid and binding, and the judge stands in the husband's place to effect a divorce, so it is attributed to the husband, making it a talaq. The ruling concludes by stating that the free woman requests separation; for a slave, the master requests.

Key Terms
العنين (al-‘innin): A man who is unable to have intercourse due to impotence or defect.
التأجيل (al-ta’jeel): The one-year deferral given to the impotent husband to consummate the marriage.
الطلاق البائن (al-talaq al-ba’in): A divorce that is irrevocable, ending the marriage immediately without right to return during iddat without a new contract.
التفريق (al-tafriq): The judge's decree of separation when the husband refuses to divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is required for the separation of the wife from an impotent husband after one year?
A) Automatic separation without any action.
B) The wife must pronounce divorce herself.
C) The judge's decree if the husband refuses to divorce.
D) The husband must give a triple divorce.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives the wife of an impotent husband the right to separation after one year, but the later relied-upon position requires a judge's decree, not automatic separation.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Nature of Separation: Talaq Bain vs. Faskh
Inter-madhhab dispute on the nature of separation for impotence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi position (talaq bain) and the Shafi'i/Ahmad position (faskh) regarding separation for impotence, and identify the practical consequences of each view.

Core Idea
The divorce for impotence is a talaq bain because the judge acts for the husband, not an annulment from the wife's side.

While the first lesson focused on the mechanism of separation (judge's decree vs automatic), this lesson addresses the legal nature of the separation itself. The Hanafi school holds that when a judge decrees separation due to impotence, it is a single irrevocable divorce (talaq bain). In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad consider it an annulment (faskh). Understanding this difference is critical because it affects how many divorces remain, whether the wife must observe iddat, and the possibility of remarriage.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the nature of separation
According to Hanafis, the separation for impotence is a talaq bain (irrevocable divorce). The text says: 'Then the separation is a irrevocable divorce according to us' (ثم الفرقة طلقة بائنة عندنا).
This means it counts as one divorce, and the husband must remarry her with a new contract if they wish to reconcile.
2
Identify the opposing view of Shafi'i and Ahmad
Shafi'i and Ahmad consider it a faskh (annulment). The text states: 'while according to al-Shafi'i and Ahmad it is annulment because it is a separation from her side' (وعند الشافعي وأحمد هي فسخ؛ لأنه فرقة من جهتها).
Faskh does not count toward the three divorces and is seen as a dissolution of the marriage from the beginning.
3
Understand the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is that the separation is attributed to the husband. The judge substitutes for the husband because the husband had an obligation to retain or release. When he fails, the judge acts on his behalf. Therefore, the act of separation is from the husband's side, making it a talaq. The text says: 'the obligation on him is retention, so when it fails, release is obligatory. So when he refrained, the judge took his place, so the act is attributed to him' (لنا أن هذه الفرقة من جهته؛ لأن الواجب عليه الإمساك، فإذا فات وجب التسريح، فلما امتنع هو قام القاضي مقامه، فكان الفعل منسوباً إليه).
Additionally, the marriage is valid and binding, and such a marriage does not admit faskh except by divorce.
4
Analyze the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
If it is talaq bain: the wife must observe iddat, it counts as one divorce (so two more remain), and they can remarry with a new contract. If it is faskh: some say no iddat? Actually iddat is still required for the wife after separation from a valid marriage, but the key difference is that faskh does not count toward the three divorces. This means the husband could marry her again without the divorce counting against the limit.
The text itself does not elaborate on all consequences, but the thamarah al-khilaf is derived from the nature of each legal categorization.
5
Apply the Hanafi ruling to a modern scenario
In a Hanafi court today, a judge decreeing separation for impotence would issue a talaq bain, not an annulment. This affects the couple's status post-separation.
The mufti must be aware that other schools may treat it differently if the couple later seeks reconciliation.
