Overlapping Iddah Due to Shubha Intercourse: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling that two iddahs from shubha intercourse overlap, with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on overlapping iddahs from shubha intercourse and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using purpose-based reasoning.

Core Idea
Two iddahs from shubha overlap because one waiting period suffices to ascertain purity of the womb.

When a woman already in an iddah is copulated with under a mistaken belief of legality (shubha), a second iddah becomes obligatory. The Hanafi school holds that these two iddahs overlap concurrently, while the Shafi'i school requires sequential completion. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school rules that the two iddahs overlap: the same menstrual cycles or months count for both simultaneously.
The passage states: 'وَتَدَاخَلَتَا' (and they overlap).
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the iddahs do not overlap; they must be observed sequentially—first the original, then the new one.
The passage says: 'وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ: لَا تَتَدَاخَلَانِ'.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argument is that each iddah is an independent obligation (haqq wajib) and thus cannot be fulfilled by the same period.
Opposing dalil: 'لِأَنَّهُمَا حَقَّانِ وَاجِبَانِ' (they are two obligatory rights).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is teleological: the purpose of iddah is to verify the womb's purity (barā'at al-rahim), and this purpose is achieved by one waiting period, so overlap suffices.
Hanafi dalil: 'وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْعِدَّةَ شُرِعَتْ لِتَعَرُّفِ بَرَاءَةِ الرَّحِمِ'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is seen in the widow example: Hanafi allows her month-based iddah to cover both, while Shafi'i requires completing the death-iddah first then a new menses-based iddah.
The passage gives this example to illustrate the overlap rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَتَجِبُ عِدَّةٌ أُخْرَى بِوَطْءِ الْمُعْتَدَّةِ بِشُبْهَةٍ، وَتَدَاخَلَتَا، وَيَكُونُ مَا تَرَاهُ الْمَرْأَةُ مِنَ الدَّمِ مُحْتَسَبًا مِنْهُمَا جَمِيعًا، وَإِذَا انْقَضَتِ الْعِدَّةُ الْأُولَى وَلَمْ تَكْمُلِ الثَّانِيَةُ، فَعَلَيْهَا إِتْمَامُ الْعِدَّةِ الثَّانِيَةِ. وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ: لَا تَتَدَاخَلَانِ، سَوَاءٌ كَانَتَا مِنْ جِنْسٍ وَاحِدٍ بِأَنْ كَانَتَا بِحَيْضٍ أَوْ أَشْهُرٍ، أَوْ مِنْ جِنْسَيْنِ بِأَنْ كَانَتْ إِحْدَاهُمَا بِحَيْضٍ وَالْأُخْرَى بِالْأَشْهُرِ، بَلْ تُتِمُّ الْأُولَى ثُمَّ تَشْرَعُ فِي الثَّانِيَةِ؛ لِأَنَّهُمَا حَقَّانِ وَاجِبَانِ فَلَا تَتَدَاخَلَانِ. وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْعِدَّةَ شُرِعَتْ لِتَعَرُّفِ بَرَاءَةِ الرَّحِمِ، وَهَذَا الْغَرَضُ يَحْصُلُ مَعَ التَّدَاخُلِ. وَلَوْ كَانَتْ مُعْتَدَّةَ الْوَفَاةِ فَوُطِئَتْ بِشُبْهَةٍ تَعْتَدُّ بِالْأَشْهُرِ، وَيُحْتَسَبُ مَا تَرَاهُ مِنَ الْحَيْضِ فِيهَا مِنَ الْعِدَّةِ الثَّانِيَةِ تَحْقِيقًا لِلتَّدَاخُلِ بِقَدْرِ الْإِمْكَانِ.
And another iddah becomes obligatory by intercourse with a woman in iddah under shubha (mistaken belief), and the two (iddahs) overlap, and what the woman sees of blood is counted from both of them together. And if the first iddah ends and the second has not been completed, then she must complete the second iddah. Al-Shafi'i said: they do not overlap, whether they are of the same type (both by menses or months) or of different types (one by menses, the other by months); rather she completes the first then begins the second, because they are two obligatory rights so they do not overlap. Our (Hanafi) proof is that the iddah was prescribed to ascertain the purity of the womb, and this purpose is achieved with overlap. And if a woman was observing the iddah of death and then was copulated with under shubha, she observes iddah by months, and the menses she sees during it are counted from the second iddah, to achieve overlap as much as possible.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage deals with a situation where a woman who is already in an iddah (either from divorce or death) is unlawfully copulated with by a man under a mistaken belief of a valid marriage or ownership (shubha). This second intercourse imposes another iddah. The Hanafi ruling is that the two iddahs overlap (tadakhul): the menstrual cycles she experiences count for both simultaneously. If the first iddah ends before the second is complete, she must complete the remaining cycles of the second iddah. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that each iddah is an independent obligation and must be fulfilled sequentially. The Hanafi position is based on the purpose of iddah: it is to ensure the womb is free from pregnancy. Since one period of waiting can achieve this for both possible pregnancies, overlap is sufficient. The text also gives an example of a widow in her four-month-and-ten-day iddah who is copulated with under shubha: she continues with the month-based iddah, and any menses she sees during those months count toward the second (menses-based) iddah, to achieve as much overlap as possible. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah): A situation where intercourse occurs under a mistaken but plausible belief of legality (e.g., a man copulates with a woman thinking she is his wife or slave).
تداخل (tadākhul): Overlap or merger of two legal obligations (here, two iddahs) such that one period of waiting fulfills both.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman is in her iddah of death (four months and ten days). During this time, a man cohabits with her under shubhah. According to the Hanafi school, how does she complete her iddahs?
A) She completes the death iddah first, then begins a new iddah of three menses
B) The two iddahs overlap; she continues with months, and any menses during that time count for the second iddah
C) She must start a new iddah from the day of shubhah intercourse, ignoring the previous iddah
D) She only needs to observe one iddah because the second is invalid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when two iddahs are triggered by shubha intercourse with a woman already in iddah, the iddahs overlap because their common purpose—verifying the womb's purity—can be achieved simultaneously.

Beginning of Iddah After Divorce, Death, and Invalid Marriage
Ruling on when iddah begins: immediately after divorce, death, or separation in invalid marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when the iddah begins for divorce, death, and invalid marriage, and explain the Hanafi ruling on the wife's claim of completed iddah.

Core Idea
The iddah begins immediately upon divorce or death, and for invalid marriage upon separation or resolve to abandon intercourse.

This lesson clarifies the starting point of the waiting period (iddah) in three key scenarios. Understanding this is fundamental because it affects the calculation of the iddah term and determines when a woman may remarry. We will also address a common dispute when the wife claims her iddah has ended and the husband denies it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Recognize the three cases: divorce (talaq), death of husband, and invalid marriage (nikah fasid). For each, there is a distinct trigger for the start of iddah.
These are the only three situations that impose an iddah in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Understand immediacy for valid divorce and death
For a valid divorce and for death, the iddah begins immediately at the moment of pronouncement or death, regardless of the woman's awareness. This is a key Hanafi ruling.
3
Note the special trigger for fasid marriage
In an invalid marriage, the iddah does not start automatically. It begins either upon formal separation (tafriq) or when the husband explicitly resolves to stop intercourse with her (e.g., by saying 'I leave you').
Mere cessation of intercourse without an explicit resolve is insufficient.
4
Examine the dispute over the wife's claim
If the wife claims her iddah has ended and the husband denies it, but the time that has passed could possibly accommodate the iddah, the wife's claim is given weight in Hanafi view.
This is based on the principle that iddah is a fixed term that passes regardless of awareness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَبْدَأُ الْعِدَّةِ بَعْدَ الطَّلَاقِ وَالْمَوْتِ وَفِي النِّكَاحِ الْفَاسِدِ بَعْدَ التَّفْرِيقِ أَوِ الْعَزْمِ عَلَى تَرْكِ وَطْئِهَا. وَإِنْ قَالَتْ: مَضَتْ عِدَّتِي وَكَذَّبَهَا الزَّوْجُ، وَالْمُدَّةُ تَحْتَمِلُ ذَلِكَ.
And the beginning of the iddah is after divorce and death, and in an invalid marriage after separation or the resolve to abandon intercourse with her. And if she says: 'My iddah has passed,' and the husband denies her, and the time period allows that (possibility).
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage states the general principle for when the waiting period (iddah) begins. For a valid divorce (talaq), the iddah starts immediately upon the pronouncement of divorce. For death of the husband, the iddah starts immediately upon the death, even if the wife is not aware of it. For an invalid marriage (nikah fasid), the iddah does not begin automatically; it begins either when the couple is formally separated by a judge (tafriq) or when the man resolves to stop having intercourse with her (e.g., by saying 'I leave you' or 'I intend to stop'). The mere cessation of intercourse without an explicit indication is not sufficient. The text also addresses a dispute: if the wife claims her iddah has ended but the husband denies it, and the time that has passed could possibly accommodate the iddah (e.g., three months for a divorcee), the statement of the wife is given consideration? Actually the text says 'and the time period allows that' – it implies that if the possible duration has elapsed, her claim is acceptable even if the husband denies it, because the iddah is a waiting period that does not require knowledge of its passage. This reflects the Hanafi view that iddah is an 'ajal' (fixed term) that passes regardless of the woman's awareness.

Key Terms
مبدأ العدة (mabda' al-'iddah): The starting point of the waiting period; for divorce and death it is immediate, for fasid marriage it is upon separation or explicit intention to stop intercourse.
النكاح الفاسد (al-nikāḥ al-fāsid): A marriage contract that is invalid due to a missing condition or prohibition, but has been consummated (according to Hanafi, it imposes iddah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the iddah begin for a woman whose husband dies, according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only when she learns of the death
B) Immediately upon the husband's death
C) After the funeral
D) When she starts menstruating

Key Takeaway
The iddah begins immediately upon divorce or death, and only upon separation or resolve in an invalid marriage, with the wife's claim of completion accepted if the time allows.

Overlapping Iddahs: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Ruling on overlapping iddahs due to shubha, with Shafi'i rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on tadakhul of iddahs, state the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi proof based on the purpose of iddah.

Core Idea
Two iddahs can overlap because their purpose is to ascertain womb purity, which is satisfied regardless of overlap.

In this lesson, we examine a practical scenario: a woman already observing iddah is cohabited with under shubha. Does she observe two separate iddahs consecutively, or can they overlap? The Hanafi school permits overlap (tadakhul), while Imam al-Shafi'i requires separation. We will analyze the proofs on both sides and understand the practical consequences of each view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The two iddahs overlap; what is seen of blood or months counts for both simultaneously. The passage states: 'وتداخلتا، والمرئي منهما، وتتم الثانية إن تمت الأولى.'
The meaning of tadakhul is that when the first iddah completes, the second is completed with whatever remains.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the iddahs do not overlap, whether they are of the same type or different types. She must complete the first then begin the second.
Ahmad ibn Hanbal agrees with overlap only when both iddahs arise from one cause (e.g., both from a husband).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Each iddah is an independent right (haqq) that must be fulfilled separately; they cannot be performed simultaneously.
The Shafi'i argument is based on the idea that obligations are individual and cannot be merged.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi proof is based on the purpose (illah) of iddah: to know the purity of the womb (barā'at al-rahim). This purpose is achieved with overlap; the total waiting period suffices.
The Hanafis illustrate with a widow in 'iddat al-wafāt: she observes months, and any menstruation counts for the second iddah as much as possible.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: under Hanafi, total waiting period is the same as the first iddah (e.g., three months if both are by months). Under Shafi'i, she must complete the first then start a new full second iddah, doubling the time.
This is a significant difference in practice, affecting the woman's ability to remarry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتجب عدة أخرى بوطء المعتدة بشبهة، وتداخلتا، والمرئي منهما، وتتم الثانية إن تمت الأولى. وتجب عدة أخرى أي إذا وطئ المعتدة بشبهة فعليها عدة أخرى، وتداخلت العدتان ويكون ما تراه المرأة من الدم محتسباً منهما جميعاً، وإذا انقضت العدة الأولى ولم تكمل الثانية، فعليها إتمام العدة الثانية، فإن كان الوطء العدة الأولى فحاضت حيضتين بعدها تمت الأولى، ووجب عليها أن الثانية تتم بحيضة ثالثة، وهذا معنى التداخل. وقال الشافعي: لا تتداخلان، سواء كانتا من جنس واحد بأن كانت بحيض أو أشهر، أو من جنسين بأن كانت إحداهما بحيض والأخرى بالأشهر، بل تتم الأولى ثم تشرع في الثانية؛ لأنهما حقان واجبان فلا تتداخلان. وإن وجبتا من واحد بأن وطئها زوجها وهي طلاق تتداخلان وبه قال أحمد. ولنا أن العدة شرعت لتعرف براءة الرحم، وهذا الغرض يحصل مع التداخل، ولو كانت معتدة الوفاة فوطئت بشبهة تعتد بالأشهر، ويحتسب ما تراه من الحيض فيها من العدة الثانية تحقيقاً للتداخل بقدر الإمكان.
And another waiting period becomes obligatory due to intercourse with a woman in her waiting period under shubha, and the two waiting periods overlap, and what is seen of blood counts for both of them, and the second is completed if the first has been completed. And another waiting period becomes obligatory, i.e., if a woman in her waiting period is cohabited with under shubha, then she owes another waiting period, and the two waiting periods overlap, and what the woman sees of blood is counted for both of them. And when the first waiting period ends but the second is not completed, she must complete the second waiting period. If the intercourse occurred after the first waiting period had started and she menstruated two times after it, the first is completed, and she must complete the second with a third menstruation. This is the meaning of overlapping. Al-Shafi'i said: They do not overlap, whether they are of the same type, like by menstruation or months, or of different types, like one by menstruation and the other by months. Rather, she completes the first, then begins the second because they are two obligatory rights, so they do not overlap. And if they are obligatory from one cause, like if her husband cohabits with her while she is in her waiting period from divorce, they overlap, and Ahmad said the same. And our proof is that the waiting period was legislated to know the purity of the womb, and this purpose is achieved with overlapping. And if a widow in her waiting period of death is cohabited with under shubha, she observes her waiting period by months, and what she sees of menstruation is counted within it for the second waiting period, effecting overlapping as much as possible.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on overlapping iddahs (waiting periods) when a woman already in iddah is cohabited with under shubha (uncertainty). The passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i, with Imam Ahmad aligning with the Hanafi view. The text first states the ruling: an additional iddah becomes obligatory, and the two iddahs overlap such that blood seen counts for both. If the first iddah ends before the second is complete, she must complete the second. The commentary explains the method: if the first iddah was by menstruation and after the shubha intercourse she completes two menstruations, the first iddah ends, and she then completes the second with a third menstruation. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that since each iddah is an independent obligatory right, they cannot overlap; she must complete one then begin the next, regardless of whether they are of the same or different types. The Hanafi response is based on the underlying purpose (illah) of iddah: to establish the purity of the womb (barā'at al-rahim). Since this purpose is fulfilled by the waiting period regardless of overlapping, there is no need for separate non-overlapping periods. The Hanafis illustrate this with the case of a widow whose iddah is by months: if she is cohabited with under shubha, she continues her months-based iddah, and any menstruation she experiences is counted towards the second iddah (due to the shubha), thus achieving overlap as much as possible. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, and the muftā bihi (operative position) is the Hanafi view favouring overlap.

Key Terms
عدد (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce, death of husband, or termination of a marriage, to ascertain the purity of the womb.
تداخل (tadakhul): The overlapping of two iddahs such that the same period of time or the same menstruations count for both.
شبهة (shubha): A situation of uncertainty where intercourse occurs under the belief it is lawful, e.g., a man finds a woman on his bed and believes she is his wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a woman in iddah from divorce is cohabited with under shubha, how is her second iddah completed?
A) She must complete the first iddah then start a new second iddah.
B) The two iddahs overlap; if the first ends after two menstruations, she completes the second with one more.
C) She only needs to complete one iddah because the second is not valid.
D) The second iddah is completely separate and must be observed after the first.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits tadakhul of iddahs because the purpose of iddah – establishing womb purity – is satisfied by the total period, regardless of overlap.

Ruling on Marrying a Mu'taddah and Divorcing Before Consummation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr and iddah for remarriage during iddah followed by pre-consummation divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar) on mahr and iddah for this scenario and evaluate the qiyas that supports the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The first marriage's iddah creates 'possession' making a subsequent divorce treated as after consummation.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute. If a man divorces his wife irrevocably, remarries her during iddah, and divorces again before consummation, what are the mahr and iddah obligations? The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) require full mahr and a new iddah, while Muhammad and Zufar offer dissenting views. The key is the analogy to a usurper purchasing usurped goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The case: a man divorces his wife bainan (irrevocably), then marries her again during her iddah with a valid contract, then divorces her before consummation (no seclusion or intercourse).
The second divorce occurs before any new physical relationship.
2
State the positions of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)
They say: full mahr (as in a consummated marriage) and a new independent iddah (mubtada'ah). This is the mufta bihi.
They treat the divorce as after consummation due to the ongoing possession from the first marriage.
3
State the opposing positions
Muhammad says: half mahr and completion of the first iddah (since divorce before consummation). Zufar says: no iddah at all (first iddah cancelled by remarriage, second not triggered).
Muhammad's view is based on the default rule for pre-consummation divorce; Zufar sees no basis for a new iddah.
4
Analyze the shaykhs' dalil: the qiyas of the usurper
The shaykhs argue that the first intercourse gave the husband 'possession' (qabd) of the wife, and the iddah is the remaining effect. When he remarries, this existing possession serves as the possession due under the new contract, just as a usurper who buys the usurped item becomes owner by contract while already in possession.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) because the possession is not physical but legal.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its authority
The view of the two shaykhs is adopted in the fatwa (Mustakhlas, Fath). The tarjih is based on the strength of the analogy and the need to protect the woman's rights.
This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو نكح معتدته فطلقها قبل الوطء وجب مهر تام وعدة مبتدأة أي كامل عليه أي للمرأة معتدته بأن كان طلقها بما دون الثلاث ثم تزوجها في العدة. (ط) قبل الوطء أي قبل الدخول بها وقبل الخلوة. (ط، ع) وجب مهر تام وعدة مبتدأة : [ أي مستقلة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف (ع)] أي إذا طلق الرجل امرأته طلاقاً بائناً ثم تزوجها في العدة نكاحاً صحيحاً ثم طلقها قبل الدخول، فعليه مهر كامل سوى الأول، وعليها عدة مستقلة غير العدة الأولى، وهذا عند الشيخين، وقال محمد لها نصف المهر، وعليها إتمام العدة الأولى؛ لأن هذا طلاق قبل الدخول، فلا يوجب كمال المهر، ولا استئناف العدة، غير أن إكمال العدة الأولى واجب بالطلاق الأول فلا يرتفع الوجوب في الطلاق الثاني؛ وقال زفر الله لا عدة عليها أصلاً؛ لأن الأولى سقطت بالتزوج فلا يعود، والثانية لم تجب؛ لأنه طلقت قبل المسيس، وقول زفر محله هو ا ولهما: أن الوطء قبض، وهي مقبوضة في يده بالقبض الأول؛ لبقاء أثره وهو العدة، فإذا عقد عليها ثانياً وهي مقبوضة في يده ناب القبض الأول عن القبض المستحق بالثاني كالغاصب إذا اشترى المغصوب وهو في يده قابضاً بمجرد العقد، فكان طلاقاً بعد الدخول، وقيدنا التزوج الثاني بالنكاح الصحيح؛ لأنه إذا كان الأول صحيحاً، والثاني فاسداً لا يلزم المهر ولا العدة إجماعاً، بخلاف العكس، فإنه بمنزلة ما لو كان كلاهما صحيحاً. (مستخلص، فتح)
And if he marries his mu'taddah and divorces her before intercourse, a full mahr and a new iddah are obligatory. i.e. complete upon him, for the woman. His mu'taddah meaning he had divorced her with less than three and then married her in the iddah. (Tahawi) Before intercourse i.e. before entry and before seclusion. (Tahawi, 'Ayni) Full mahr and new iddah are obligatory: i.e. independent according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. ('Ayni) i.e. if a man divorces his wife a bail divorce, then marries her in the iddah a valid marriage, then divorces her before consummation, then a full mahr besides the first, and a separate iddah different from the first, and this is the view of the two shaykhs. Muhammad said she gets half the mahr and she completes the first iddah; because this is a divorce before consummation, so it does not necessitate full mahr nor a new iddah, except that completing the first iddah is obligatory by the first divorce so it does not rise in the second divorce. Zufar said there is no iddah on her at all because the first fell by marriage and does not return, and the second did not become obligatory because she was divorced before touch. And Zufar's saying is his view. And for them (the two imams): that intercourse is taking possession, and she is in his possession by the first possession due to the remaining effect which is the iddah, so when he contracts with her a second time while she is in his possession, the first possession takes the place of the possession due by the second, like the usurper when he buys the usurped item while it is in his hand, then he becomes possessor by mere contract, so it is a divorce after consummation. And we restricted the second marriage to valid marriage because if the first is valid and the second is invalid, neither mahr nor iddah apply by consensus, contrary to the reverse; for it is like the case when both are valid. (Mustakhlas, Fath).
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The ruling: if a man divorces his wife bainan (irrevocably), then marries her during her iddah with a valid contract, then divorces again before consummation, what is the mahr and iddah? The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say: full mahr (as in consummated marriage) and a new independent iddah. Muhammad says: half mahr and completing the first iddah. Zufar says: no iddah at all. The proof for the shaykhs: the first marriage's intercourse is considered 'possession' (qabd), and its effect (the iddah) continues, so when he remarries, the first possession serves for the second, making the divorce after consummation. Analogy: a usurper who buys the usurped item becomes possessor immediately by the contract. The correct (mufta bihi) is the view of the two shaykhs.

Key Terms
مبتدأة (mubtada'ah): A new separate iddah, independent of the previous one.
وطء (wat'): Sexual intercourse.
قبض (qabd): Legal possession; in this context, the husband's authority over his wife established by the first marriage's intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if a man divorces his wife bainan, remarries her in her iddah, and divorces again before consummation, what is the mahr?
A) Half the mahr prescribed in the second marriage.
B) Full mahr.
C) No mahr.
D) Mahr equal to the first marriage.

Key Takeaway
When a man remarries his mu'taddah and divorces before consummation, the mufta bihi requires full mahr and a new iddah, based on the qiyas of the usurper and the doctrine of ongoing possession.

Dhimmi Divorce and the Absence of Iddah
Ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on iddah for dhimmis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on iddah for dhimmis, explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A dhimmi divorce does not impose iddah because the law does not bind those outside its address.

The question of whether a dhimmi woman must observe iddah after divorce by her dhimmi husband is a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa holds that no iddah is required, while his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, argue that it is necessary. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each view and establishes the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling as given in the opening of the passage: no iddah for a dhimmi woman divorced by a dhimmi husband.
This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
State that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require iddah. They argue that separation after consummation in Dar al-Islam necessitates iddah, analogous to death.
They rely on the apparent generality of separation after consummation.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing proof
Abu Hanifa responds that iddah is a right of Shari'ah, not of the husband, and dhimmis are not addressed by Shari'ah obligations. Moreover, the husband does not believe in iddah.
The principle 'we leave them to their religion' supports this.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if no iddah, the woman may remarry immediately (if not pregnant); if iddah is required, she must wait three menstrual cycles.
Pregnancy triggers a consensus waiting period until delivery.
5
Identify the tarjih and mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Abu Hanifa's view, as supported by Fath.
This is the mufta bihi within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو طلق ذمي ذمية لم تعتد. ذمية أي غير حامل وكذا إذا مات عنها زوجها. (ط) لم تعتد : [ أي لا يجب عليها العدة إذا كانت لا تجب في معتقده عند الإمام (ع)] أي لا يجب عليها العدة؛ لأنها إما أن تجب حقاً للشرع أو للزوج، ولا وجه للأول؛ لأنها غير مخاطبة بحقوق الشرع، ولا للثاني؛ لأن الزوج لا يعتقده، وقد أمرنا بتركهم وما يدينون، ولو كانت حاملاً لا تتزوج بالإجماع حتى تضع حملها؛ لأن الحمل ثابت النسب من الذمي، وقالا عليها العدة؛ لأن هذه الفرقة وقعت بعد الدخول في دار الإسلام بسبب التباين فيجب عليها العدة كما لو وقعت بسبب آخر كالموت، وله قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ أَنْ تَنْكِحُوهُنَّ﴾ وقول المصنف رحله: "طلق ذمي"؛ لأن المسلم لو كان تحته ذمية وطلقها وجبت عليها العدة طلاقه ومن وفاته أيضاً بلا خلاف ولو كانت لا تدينها؛ لأن العدة حق الزوج ومعتقده، والحاصل أنه لو تزوج الذمية المطلقة ذميّ أو مسلم في فور طلاق زوجها الذمي جاز. And if a dhimmi divorces a dhimmiyyah, she does not observe iddah. (Meaning non-pregnant, and likewise if her husband dies on her). (Tahawi) She does not observe iddah: i.e. iddah is not obligatory upon her if it is not obligatory in her belief according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). ('Ayni) It is not obligatory upon her because it is either a right of the Shari'ah or a right of the husband. The first is not applicable because she is not addressed by Shari'ah obligations; the second because the husband does not believe in it, and we are commanded to leave them and their religion. If she is pregnant, she cannot marry by consensus until she gives birth because the lineage is established from the dhimmi. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: she must observe iddah because this separation occurred after consummation in the abode of Islam due to apostasy, so iddah is obligatory upon her just as if it occurred due to another cause like death. And for him is the verse: 'And there is no sin upon you that you marry them' (al-Mumtahinah:10). And the statement of the author: 'dhimmi divorces' because if a Muslim has a dhimmi wife and divorces her, iddah is obligatory upon her from his divorce and also from his death without disagreement even if she does not believe in it, because iddah is the right of the husband and his belief. The conclusion: if a dhimmi or Muslim marries the divorced dhimmiyyah immediately after her dhimmi husband's divorce, it is permissible. (Fath) Absolutely.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on the iddah of a dhimmi woman divorced by her dhimmi husband. Abu Hanifa holds no iddah because the woman is not obligated by Islamic law (she is not a Muslim addressed by Shari'ah), and the husband does not believe in iddah. We are instructed to leave them to their own religious practices. However, if she is pregnant, she cannot remarry until delivery by ijma' due to lineage. The two students argue that since the divorce occurs in Dar al-Islam after consummation, iddah is required as a right of the husband (even if he doesn't believe) just as in the case of death. They cite the Quranic verse about marrying believing women (but the text is truncated). The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa, as indicated by the text's opening 'she does not observe iddah' and the support from Fath.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Islamic rule with a pact of protection.
عدة (iddah): The waiting period after divorce or death before remarriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a dhimmi woman divorced by her dhimmi husband is not required to observe iddah, and she may remarry immediately unless pregnant.

Ihdaad: Obligatory Mourning for Every Mu'taddah
Definition and rulings of mourning period for divorced and widowed women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ihdaad for divorced and widowed women, identify the elements of ihdaad and exceptions, and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i/Malik.

Core Idea
Ihdaad is wajib for every mu'taddah – both divorced and widowed – as a right of the Shari'ah.

This lesson unpacks the definition and obligations of ihdaad (mourning) during the iddah period. You will learn what actions are prohibited, what exceptions exist, and why the Hanafi school extends ihdaad to divorced women despite disagreement from the Shafi'i and Maliki schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify that ihdaad is a wajib obligation upon all women in iddah (both divorce and death) and that it is a right of Shari'ah, not waivable by the husband.
2
List the elements of ihdaad
List what must be refrained from: adornment (jewelry, silk, combing), perfume, kohl, oil, henna, and note the exception: legitimate excuse (e.g., medical need).
The source uses 'except with an excuse' as a general qualifier.
3
Examine the dalil
Analyze the general hadith forbidding henna for the mu'taddah (Nasa'i), which the Hanafis use as evidence that the prohibition applies to all mu'taddat, including divorced women.
The hadith is general ('amm') and thus includes both categories.
4
Understand the dispute
Compare with the Shafi'i/Maliki view that ihdaad is only for widows, and understand the Hanafi response: the reason ('illah) is grief over loss of marital blessing, not just the husband's death; separation can be more severe.
The Hanafi response also notes that a woman may wash her husband before divorce but not after, indicating greater severance.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Recognize that the practical difference is that in the Hanafi school, a divorced woman must refrain from adornment, while in the Shafi'i/Maliki school she may adorn herself.
This affects daily practice during the iddah period.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان الإحداد تحد معتدة البت والموت بترك الزينة والطيب والكحل والدهن إلا بعذر، والحنّاء. فصل: لما ذكر العدة ومن عليها أردفه بذكر ما يجب فيها على المعتدّات، فإنه في المرتبة الثانية من أصل وجوبها، ولو أمرها المطلق أو الميت بترك الإحداد لم يحل لها ذلك؛ لأنه حق الشرع، وقوله: "تحدّ" . حدت المرأة حداداً . من فهي حاد من باب "نصر" و"ضرب"، وأحدّت إحداداً فهي محد، ومعنى "تحد" تتأسف، والحد المنع، الحداد؛ لأن المرأة منعت من الزينة، ومنه سمي البواب حداداً. (فتح، عيني) الإحداد أو الحد: وهو ترك زينة المرأة وخضابها بعد وفات الزوج. (مس) معتدة البت: [ أي القطع، وأراد به معتدة الطلاق البائن سواء كانت حرة أو أمة (ع)] أي البائن، ومنه لفرقة بخيار الجب والعنة، وكذا إذا وقعت الفرقة بإبائه عن الإسلام فلا يحل الإحداد لمن مات أبوها أو ابنها أو أمها وأخوها، وإنما هو في الزوج خاصة سواء كانت حرة أو غيرها؛ لأنها مخاطبة بحقوق الشرع فيما ليس فيه إبطال حق المولى بخلاف المنع من الخروج؛ لأن فيه إبطال حقه، وحق العبد مقدم لحاجته. (فتح) الموت أي وتحد معتدة الموت بلا خلاف. (ع) بترك الزينة: أي الكائنة بحلي أو حرير أو امتشاط أو التزين بالجواهر كلها، ويلبس الحرير وغيره من الثياب المصبوغة، وقوله: "و"الطيب" أي لا تستعمله ولا تحضر عمله ولا تتجر فيه وإن لم يكن لها كسب إلا فيه، والمراد من التجارة فيه تعاطيها بنفسها، وقوله: "والكحل "والدهن" هما بفتح استعمال الكحل والدهن، والاسم فيهما بالضم، وقوله : إلا بعذر قيد في الكل فيجوز لها لبس الحرير للحكة والقمل والثوب المصبوغ لعدم وجود غيره، وكذا يجوز استعمال الطيب والدهن للتداوي والكحل للرمد ،ونحوه، وكذا الثوب المصبوغ أسود؛ لأنه لا يقصد به الزينة، وكذا لو كان الثياب خلقاً . بحيث لا تقع به الزينة فلا بأس به. وقال الشافعي ومالك لا حداد في المبتوتة؛ لورود النص في المتوفى عنها زوجها؛ ولأنه وجب إظهاراً للتأسف على وفاة زوج وفى بعهدها إلى مماته وقد أوحشها بالإبانة فلا تتأسف بفوته، ولنا: أنه وجب إظهاراً للتأسف على فوات نعمة النكاح الذي هو سبب لصونها وكفاية مؤنتها، والإبانة أقطع لها من الموت حتى كان لها أن تغسله ميتاً قبل الإبانة لا بعدها، وإنما لم يجب على الرجل مع أنه فاته نعمة النكاح؛ لأن الحداد تبع للعدة؛ ولهذا لا يحل لها ذلك على غير الزوج كالولد لفقد العدة، ولنا أيضاً ما روي أنه عليها نهى المعتدة أن تختضب بالحناء، رواه النسائي، وهو مطلق فيتناول المطلقة. (فتح عيني) والكحل: أي وترك الكحل بفتح الكاف وهو استعمال الكحل بالضم (ع) والدهن: أي وترك الدهن بفتح الدال مصدر دهن يدهن وبالضم الاسم. (ع) والحناء : أي وترك الحناء؛ لأنه طيب كما في حديث النسائي. (ع)
Chapter on explaining ihdaad. She observes ihdaad (mourning) as a mu'taddah of absolute divorce and death by leaving adornment, perfume, kohl, oil, except with an excuse, and henna. Chapter: When he mentioned iddah and those upon whom it is obligatory, he followed it by mentioning what is obligatory upon the mu'taddaat, for it is in the second degree from the origin of its obligation. And if the divorcer or the deceased ordered her to leave ihdaad, it is not permissible for her because it is a right of the Shari'ah. And his saying: 'tahiddu'... the woman performed ihdaad... from the pattern of 'nasara' and 'daraba', and 'ahaddat' she is 'muhidd'. And the meaning of 'tahiddu' is to mourn, and 'hadd' is prevention, because the woman is prevented from adornment, hence the gatekeeper is called 'haddad'. (Fath, 'Ayni) Ihdaad or hadd: it is leaving woman's adornment and dyeing after the husband's death. (Muslim) Mu'taddah of 'al-batt': i.e. cutting, meaning the mu'taddah of irrevocable divorce whether free or slave. ('Ayni) i.e. irrevocable, and includes separation by option of impotence and defect, and likewise if separation occurs due to his refusal to accept Islam. And ihdaad is not permissible for one whose father, son, mother, or brother dies; it is only for the husband especially, whether free or not, because she is addressed by the rights of Shari'ah in matters that do not nullify the right of her master unlike prohibition of exiting because that nullifies his right, and the right of the slave is given precedence for his need. (Fath) Death i.e. and the mu'taddah of death observes ihdaad without disagreement. ('Ayni) By leaving adornment: i.e. that which is with jewelry, silk, combing, and adornment with all jewels, and she may wear silk and other dyed clothes. And his saying: 'and perfume' i.e. she should not use it, nor be present at its making, nor trade in it even if she has no livelihood except it, and the intention of trade is her personal involvement. And his saying: 'and kohl and oil' both with fatha for the act and damma for the noun. And his saying: 'except with an excuse' is a restriction for all, so it is permissible for her to wear silk for itching and lice, and dyed cloth if no other exists, and likewise use of perfume and oil for medicine, and kohl for ophthalmia and the like, and likewise black dyed cloth because it is not intended for adornment, and similarly if the clothes are worn out such that they are not for adornment, then there is no harm. And al-Shafi'i and Malik said there is no ihdaad for the mabtutah (irrevocably divorced) because the text came concerning the one whose husband died; and because it is obligated to show grief over the death of a husband who fulfilled his covenant until death, but he has alienated her by separation so she does not grieve his loss. And for us: it is obligated to show grief over the loss of the blessing of marriage which is the cause of her preservation and sufficiency of her expenses, and separation is more severe for her than death such that she could wash him dead before separation but not after. And it is not obligatory on the man even though he loses the blessing of marriage because ihdaad is subsidiary to iddah, and hence it is not permissible for her for other than the husband, like a child, due to lack of iddah. And also for us is what is narrated that the Prophet (s) forbade the mu'taddah from dyeing with henna, narrated by Nasa'i, and it is general and includes the divorced. (Fath 'Ayni) And kohl: i.e. leaving kohl with fatha on the kaf which is the act of applying kohl (with damma). ('Ayni) And oil: i.e. leaving oil with fatha on the dal as a verbal noun, and with damma the noun. ('Ayni) And henna: i.e. leaving henna because it is a perfume as in the hadith of Nasa'i. ('Ayni)
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This chapter (fasl) defines and explains ihdaad (mourning) for women in iddah. Ihdaad is obligatory for both divorced (bain) and widowed women. It consists of refraining from adornment, perfume, kohl, oil, and henna unless there is an excuse (e.g., medical need). The commentator explains that ihdaad is a right of the Shari'ah, so even if the husband or deceased ordered otherwise, she must observe it. The text then details each item and exceptions. A key dispute with Shafi'i and Malik: they say ihdaad is only for widows, not divorced. The Hanafi response: it is grief for loss of marital blessing, and separation is even more severe than death; also, the Prophet forbade henna for any mu'taddah (general evidence). Hence, the Hanafi position includes the divorced woman. The text also clarifies that ihdaad is only for the husband, not for the death of other relatives like father or son.

Key Terms
إحداد (ihdaad): The practice of a woman refraining from adornment, perfume, kohl, oil, etc., during her iddah.
معتدة البت (mu'taddah al-batt): A woman observing iddah after an irrevocable divorce (bain).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is ihdaad required?
A) Only for widows.
B) Only for divorced women.
C) For all women in iddah, whether from divorce or death.
D) Only for free women.

Key Takeaway
Ihdaad is a wajib right of Shari'ah for every woman in iddah, involving restraint from adornment, with exceptions for medical need.

Ihdad for the Mu'taddah: The Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Expansion of ihdad ruling with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ihdad for the mu'taddah, distinguish between the scope for widows and irrevocably divorced women, and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Ihdad is wajib for any woman in iddah—whether from death or ba'in divorce—because it grieves the loss of marriage's blessings.

The obligation of ihdad (mourning by abstaining from adornment) during the waiting period is settled for widows, but a dispute arises over the irrevocably divorced woman. The Hanafi school extends ihdad to her, while the Shafi'i and Maliki schools limit it to widows. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi proof and the opposing arguments, detailing what ihdad entails and its exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Define Ihdad and its Scope
Identify the linguistic and legal meaning of ihdad, and note that it applies to both iddah of death and ba'in divorce in the Hanafi school.
The text defines ihdad as abandoning adornment and dyeing after the husband's death or irrevocable divorce.
2
List the Prohibited and Permitted Acts
Distill from the text which adornments are prohibited (jewelry, silk, combing, perfume, kohl, oil, dyed clothes) and which are allowed due to necessity (medical, no alternative).
Exceptions include wearing silk for itching, using perfume for treatment, or wearing worn-out clothes not meant for adornment.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Proof
Understand the Hanafi rationale: ihdad shows grief for the loss of marriage's protection and provision; divorce cuts off benefits more permanently than death, making it a greater occasion for grief. Also cite the general hadith forbidding henna for any mu'taddah.
The hadith from Nasa'i is a general prohibition that includes the divorced woman.
4
Examine the Shafi'i/Maliki Objection and Hanafi Response
The opposing school argues that the Quran (2:234) only mentions death, and divorce alienates the woman so she does not grieve. The Hanafi response: ihdad follows the iddah, and the loss of marriage benefits is more severe in divorce.
The text also notes that the husband is not required to do ihdad because it is tied to the waiting period, which only applies to women.
5
Determine the Practical Difference (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The difference affects the daily life of a divorced woman: under Shafi'i/Maliki she may adorn herself, under Hanafi she must refrain.
This affects her remarriage prospects and social behavior during the iddah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(فتح، عيني) تحد من سمي الإحداد أو الحد: وهو ترك زينة المرأة وخضابها بعد وفات الزوج. (مس) معتدة البت: [ أي القطع، وأراد به معتدة الطلاق البائن سواء كانت حرة أو أمة (ع)] أي البائن، ومنه لفرقة بخيار الجب والعنة، وكذا إذا وقعت الفرقة بإبائه عن الإسلام فلا يحل الإحداد لمن مات أبوها أو ابنها أو أمها وأخوها، وإنما هو في الزوج خاصة سواء كانت حرة أو غيرها؛ لأنها مخاطبة بحقوق الشرع فيما ليس فيه إبطال حق المولى بخلاف المنع من الخروج؛ لأن فيه إبطال حقه، وحق العبد مقدم لحاجته. (فتح) الموت أي وتحد معتدة الموت بلا خلاف. (ع) بترك الزينة: أي الكائنة بحلي أو حرير أو امتشاط أو التزين بالجواهر كلها، ويلبس الحرير وغيره من الثياب المصبوغة، وقوله: "و"الطيب" أي لا تستعمله ولا تحضر عمله ولا تتجر فيه وإن لم يكن لها كسب إلا فيه، والمراد من التجارة فيه تعاطيها بنفسها، وقوله: "والكحل "والدهن" هما بفتح استعمال الكحل والدهن، والاسم فيهما بالضم، وقوله : إلا بعذر قيد في الكل فيجوز لها لبس الحرير للحكة والقمل والثوب المصبوغ لعدم وجود غيره، وكذا يجوز استعمال الطيب والدهن للتداوي والكحل للرمد ،ونحوه، وكذا الثوب المصبوغ أسود؛ لأنه لا يقصد به الزينة، وكذا لو كان الثياب خلقاً . بحيث لا تقع به الزينة فلا بأس به. وقال الشافعي ومالك لا حداد في المبتوتة؛ لورود النص في المتوفى عنها زوجها؛ ولأنه وجب إظهاراً للتأسف على وفاة زوج وفى بعهدها إلى مماته وقد أوحشها بالإبانة فلا تتأسف بفوته، ولنا: أنه وجب إظهاراً للتأسف على فوات نعمة النكاح الذي هو سبب لصونها وكفاية مؤنتها، والإبانة أقطع لها من الموت حتى كان لها أن تغسله ميتاً قبل الإبانة لا بعدها، وإنما لم يجب على الرجل مع أنه فاته نعمة النكاح؛ لأن الحداد تبع للعدة؛ ولهذا لا يحل لها ذلك على غير الزوج كالولد لفقد العدة، ولنا أيضاً ما روي أنه عليها نهى المعتدة أن تختضب بالحناء، رواه النسائي، وهو مطلق فيتناول المطلقة. (فتح عيني)
Section: When he mentioned the waiting period and who is obligated, he followed it by mentioning what is obligatory upon the women in waiting period, for it is in the second rank of the origin of its obligation. And if the divorcer or the deceased ordered her to abandon ihdad, it is not permissible for her to do so because it is a right of the Law. His statement: "She performs ihdad." The woman performs ihdad... meaning she expresses grief. Al-hadd means prevention, al-hidad because the woman is prevented from adornment. (Fath, Ayni) Al-ihdad or al-hadd: it is the woman's abandonment of adornment and dyeing after the death of the husband. (Misbah) Mu'taddah of al-batt: meaning the irrevocable divorce, whether free or slave. (Ayni) i.e., the irrevocable, and from it is separation by the option of impotence and castration, and likewise if separation occurs by his refusal of Islam. Ihidad is not permissible for one whose father, son, mother, or brother dies; it is only for the husband specifically, whether free or otherwise, because she is addressed by the rights of the Law in matters that do not nullify the master's right, unlike the prohibition of leaving the house, because that nullifies his right, and the slave's right is given precedence due to his need. (Fath) Death i.e., the mu'taddah of death performs ihdad without disagreement. (Ayni) By abandoning adornment: i.e., that which is by jewelry, silk, combing, or adornment with all jewels, and she may wear silk and other dyed garments. His statement: "and perfume" i.e., she should not use it, nor attend its preparation, nor trade in it even if she has no other livelihood, and the intent of trading in it is engaging in it herself. His statement: "and kohl and oil" both are with fatha referring to the act of using kohl and oil, while the noun is with dammah. His statement: "except for an excuse" is a restriction on all, so it is permissible for her to wear silk due to itching and lice, and a dyed garment if she has no other, likewise it is permissible to use perfume and oil for medical treatment, and kohl for ophthalmia and the like, likewise a black dyed garment because it is not intended for adornment, likewise if the garment is worn out such that it does not serve as adornment, there is no harm. Al-Shafi'i and Malik said: No ihdad for the irrevocably divorced woman, because the text pertains to the woman whose husband has died, and because it is prescribed to show grief over the death of a husband who fulfilled his covenant with her until his death, whereas the divorce has alienated her so she does not grieve over his loss. Our proof: It is prescribed to show grief over the loss of the blessing of marriage which is the means of her protection and provision, and separation is more severe for her than death, to the extent that she could wash him dead before separation but not after. And it is not obligatory upon the man, even though he has lost the blessing of marriage, because ihdad follows the waiting period; and therefore it is not permissible for her regarding anyone other than the husband, like a child, due to the absence of a waiting period. Also we have what is narrated that he (peace be upon him) forbade the woman in waiting period to dye with henna, narrated by al-Nasa'i, and it is general, so it includes the divorced woman. (Fath, Ayni)
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of ihdad for women in iddah. It begins by stating that the obligation of ihdad is a right of Allah, so neither the divorcer nor the deceased can exempt her. It defines ihdad as abandoning adornment. Then it specifies that ihdad is for both ba'in divorce and death iddah, and is specific to the husband; mourning for other relatives is not prescribed. The text then details what constitutes adornment: jewelry, silk, combing, perfumes, kohl, oil, and dyed clothes, with exceptions for medical needs or unavoidable circumstances. The core of the passage is an inter-madhhab dispute: Shafi'i and Malik argue that ihdad is only for widows, not irrevocably divorced women, because the Quranic verse mentions death and because divorce causes alienation. The Hanafi response is that ihdad is for the loss of the blessing of marriage, and divorce is an even greater loss; the husband is not required because ihdad follows the iddah. The Hanafis also cite a hadith from al-Nasa'i that generally prohibits henna for any woman in iddah, which includes the divorced woman.

Key Terms
الإحداد (al-ihdad): The woman's abandonment of adornment and dyeing after the death of her husband or after ba'in divorce.
البت (al-batt): The irrevocable divorce (ba'in).
المعتدة (al-mu'taddah): A woman observing the waiting period (iddah) after death of husband or divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following women is NOT required to observe ihdad?
A) A widow in iddah of death.
B) A woman in iddah of ba'in divorce.
C) A woman whose father died.
D) A woman whose husband died before consummation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires ihdad for any woman in iddah (death or ba'in divorce) as an expression of grief for the loss of marriage, and it cannot be waived by human permission.

Conditions for Ihidad: Adulthood and Islam Required
Conditions for ihdad and exemptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for ihdad (bulugh and Islam) and identify which women are exempt according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ihdad is wajib only for adult Muslim women who have lost the blessing of marriage.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa’iq continues the discussion on ihdad by specifying its conditions. While the previous section established that ihdad is required in iddah of death and ba’in divorce, here we learn that it is conditional upon the woman being an adult (baligha) and Muslim. Furthermore, several categories of women are exempt because they have not truly lost the blessing of marriage (ni‘mat al-nikah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions
The text states 'إذا كانت بالغة مسلمة' – ihdad is wajib only if the woman is adult (baligha) and Muslim. For a minor (saghira) or a non-Muslim (kafira), it is not obligatory.
The condition of adulthood is agreed upon by all schools; the condition of Islam is specific to the Hanafi view.
2
Understand exemptions for non-Muslim and minor
A non-Muslim woman is not addressed by this ruling (khitab) even if her husband was Muslim. If she converts during iddah, ihdad becomes wajib for the remaining period. A minor is not mukallaf and thus exempt by consensus.
3
List exemptions due to preserved marital blessing
Women who have not lost the blessing of marriage do not observe ihdad: umm walad (upon her master's death), woman in iddah of fasid marriage, woman penetrated by mistake (shubha), and woman in revocable (raj‘i) divorce. The reasoning: the default is permissibility of adornment, and ihdad is an exception for those who have truly lost the marital bond.
The text cites Quran 7:32 to support the permissibility of adornment.
4
Appreciate the proof structure
The proof for the general rule is the verse 'Say: Who has forbidden the adornment of Allah...' which establishes permissibility (ibaha) as the original state. Ihdad is a restriction for those who have lost the blessing of marriage. This is a talil (reasoning) based on the underlying rationale.
5
Recognize the inter-madhhab dispute
Shafi‘i and Maliki hold that ihdad is only for death iddah, not for ba‘in divorce. Hanafis extend it to ba‘in divorce because the blessing of marriage is lost in both cases, and because of the general implication of the hadith (narrated by al-Nasa'i) that forbids henna for women in iddah.
This dispute is recorded in the commentary as a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(فتح، عيني) تحد من سمي الإحداد أو الحد: وهو ترك زينة المرأة وخضابها بعد وفات الزوج. (مس) معتدة البت: [ أي القطع، وأراد به معتدة الطلاق البائن سواء كانت حرة أو أمة (ع)] أي البائن، ومنه لفرقة بخيار الجب والعنة، وكذا إذا وقعت الفرقة بإبائه عن الإسلام فلا يحل الإحداد لمن مات أبوها أو ابنها أو أمها وأخوها، وإنما هو في الزوج خاصة سواء كانت حرة أو غيرها؛ لأنها مخاطبة بحقوق الشرع فيما ليس فيه إبطال حق المولى بخلاف المنع من الخروج؛ لأن فيه إبطال حقه، وحق العبد مقدم لحاجته. (فتح) الموت أي وتحد معتدة الموت بلا خلاف. (ع) بترك الزينة: أي الكائنة بحلي أو حرير أو امتشاط أو التزين بالجواهر كلها، ويلبس الحرير وغيره من الثياب المصبوغة، وقوله: "و"الطيب" أي لا تستعمله ولا تحضر عمله ولا تتجر فيه وإن لم يكن لها كسب إلا فيه، والمراد من التجارة فيه تعاطيها بنفسها، وقوله: "والكحل "والدهن" هما بفتح استعمال الكحل والدهن، والاسم فيهما بالضم، وقوله : إلا بعذر قيد في الكل فيجوز لها لبس الحرير للحكة والقمل والثوب المصبوغ لعدم وجود غيره، وكذا يجوز استعمال الطيب والدهن للتداوي والكحل للرمد ،ونحوه، وكذا الثوب المصبوغ أسود؛ لأنه لا يقصد به الزينة، وكذا لو كان الثياب خلقاً . بحيث لا تقع به الزينة فلا بأس به. وقال الشافعي ومالك لا حداد في المبتوتة؛ لورود النص في المتوفى عنها زوجها؛ ولأنه وجب إظهاراً للتأسف على وفاة زوج وفى بعهدها إلى مماته وقد أوحشها بالإبانة فلا تتأسف بفوته، ولنا: أنه وجب إظهاراً للتأسف على فوات نعمة النكاح الذي هو سبب لصونها وكفاية مؤنتها، والإبانة أقطع لها من الموت حتى كان لها أن تغسله ميتاً قبل الإبانة لا بعدها، وإنما لم يجب على الرجل مع أنه فاته نعمة النكاح؛ لأن الحداد تبع للعدة؛ ولهذا لا يحل لها ذلك على غير الزوج كالولد لفقد العدة، ولنا أيضاً ما روي أنه عليها نهى المعتدة أن تختضب بالحناء، رواه النسائي، وهو مطلق فيتناول المطلقة. (فتح عيني) والكحل: أي وترك الكحل بفتح الكاف وهو استعمال الكحل بالضم (ع) والدهن: أي وترك الدهن بفتح الدال مصدر دهن يدهن وبالضم الاسم. (ع) والحناء : أي وترك الحناء؛ لأنه طيب كما في حديث النسائي. (ع) المعصفر : أي وترك لبس الثوب المصبوغ بالمعصفر . (ع) إن كانت بالغة مسلمة [ أي هذا الحداد واجب عليها إن كانت المرأة المعتدة بالغة فلا يجب على الصغيرة. (ع)] أي هذا الحداد واجب عليها بشرط البلوغ والإسلام، فلا يجب على الكافرة وإن أبانها مسلم أو مات عنها، إلا إذا أسلمت في خلال العدة وجب عليها في الباقي، وقالت الثلاثة عليها الحداد؛ لإطلاق النصوص، ولا على الصبية؛ لأنها غير مخاطبة اتفاقاً. (فتح) ولو أمة: متصل بما قبله و لم يوجد إلا في بعض النسخ (محشي) لا معتدة العتق [بأن أعتق أم ولده؛ لأنها ما فاتها نعمة النكاح. (ع)] أي لا تحد أم الولد؛ لأنها ما فاتها نعمة النكاح لتظهر التأسف والأصل إباحة الزينة خصوصاً في حق النساء، وقال تعالى: ﴿قُلْ مَنْ حَرَّمَ زِينَةَ اللَّهِ الَّتِي أَخْرَجَ لِعِبَادِهِ﴾ (الأعراف: ۳۲)، وقوله: "ولا معتدة النكاح الفاسد"، وكذا الموطوءة بشبهة ومعتدة طلاق رجعي ؛ لأنه لم يفتهن نعمة النكاح. (مستخلص، فتح) والنكاح ا الفاسد: أي ولا تحد أيضاً معتدة النكاح الفاسد لما مر ولا معتدة الطلاق الرجعي لقيام نعمة النكاح. (عيني)
Section: When he mentioned the waiting period and who is obligated, he followed it by mentioning what is obligatory upon the women in waiting period... (same as lesson 1 up to the dispute) ... and kohl: i.e., abandoning the use of kohl with fatha on the kaf, which is the act of using kohl, while the noun is with dammah. (Ayni) And oil: i.e., abandoning the use of oil, with fatha on the dal, verbal noun of 'dahana yadhanu', and with dammah the noun. (Ayni) And henna: i.e., abandoning henna because it is perfume as in the hadith of al-Nasa'i. (Ayni) And safflower-dyed garment: i.e., abandoning wearing a garment dyed with safflower. (Ayni) If she is an adult Muslim [i.e., this ihdad is obligatory upon her if the woman in iddah is an adult, so it is not obligatory upon a minor. (Ayni)] i.e., this ihdad is obligatory upon her on the condition of adulthood and Islam, so it is not obligatory upon a disbelieving woman even if a Muslim divorced her or died upon her, unless she accepts Islam during the iddah then it becomes obligatory upon her for the remaining period. The three imams (Abu Hanifa's companions?) said: ihdad is upon her due to the generality of the texts. And not upon a girl because she is not addressed by agreement. (Fath) 'And even if a slave': connected to the previous, but found only in some copies. (Mahashi) 'Not the mu'taddah of emancipation' [i.e., if he emancipates his umm walad, because she has not lost the blessing of marriage. (Ayni)] i.e., the umm walad does not perform ihdad because she has not lost the blessing of marriage to show grief, and the original ruling is permissibility of adornment especially for women. Allah says: 'Say: Who has forbidden the adornment of Allah which He has produced for His servants?' (7:32). And his statement: 'And not the mu'taddah of fasid marriage' and likewise the woman penetrated by mistake and the woman in iddah of revocable divorce, because they have not lost the blessing of marriage. (Mustakhlas, Fath) 'And fasid marriage': i.e., the mu'taddah of fasid marriage also does not perform ihdad due to what preceded, and neither does the mu'taddah of revocable divorce because the blessing of marriage remains. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on ihdad. After the dispute, it details the specific prohibitions: kohl, oil, henna, and safflower-dyed garments are all disallowed. It then states the conditions for ihdad: the woman must be an adult (baligha) and Muslim. Therefore, a minor girl does not observe ihdad, nor does a non-Muslim woman, even if she was married to a Muslim. However, if she converts during iddah, ihdad becomes wajib for the remaining period. The text also lists women who are exempt because they have not lost the blessing of marriage: the umm walad (slave mother of her master's child) upon her master's death, the woman in iddah of a fasid marriage, the woman penetrated by mistake (shubha), and the woman in revocable (raj'i) divorce. The reasoning is that the original ruling is permissibility of adornment, and ihdad is an exception for those who have truly lost the marital blessing. The verse from al-A'raf is cited to support the permissibility of adornment.

Key Terms
المعصفر (al-mu'asfar): A garment dyed with safflower, considered adornment and thus prohibited during ihdad.
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A slave woman who bore a child to her master; upon his death she becomes free but does not observe ihdad because she has not lost the blessing of marriage.
المبتوتة (al-mubtatta): A woman divorced irrevocably (ba'in talaq); the text discusses whether she must observe ihdad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following women is NOT required to observe ihdad?
A) A Muslim adult woman in iddah of death.
B) A Muslim adult woman in iddah of ba'in divorce.
C) A non-Muslim woman whose Muslim husband died.
D) An adult Muslim woman in iddah of revocable divorce.

Key Takeaway
Ihdad is wajib only for adult Muslim women who have lost the blessing of marriage; those still in a marital bond or non-Muslim are exempt.

Rulings on Proposals and Leaving the House During Iddah
Rules on proposing to and the movement of women in iddah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of direct proposal to a woman in iddah, distinguish ta'rid from direct proposal, and explain the ruling on a divorced woman leaving her house during iddah.

Core Idea
Direct proposal to any woman in iddah is haram; indirect hints are only for widows. A divorced woman must stay home except for clear immorality.

This lesson addresses two key rulings that safeguard the iddah period. First, the rules of marriage proposals—what is allowed and what is forbidden. Second, the restriction on a divorced woman's movement. Both are based on clear Quranic proofs and have practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
First: direct proposal (khitbah) to any woman in iddah is prohibited. However, indirect ta'rid is permitted for widows only. Second: a divorced woman in iddah must not leave her marital home day or night, unless she commits a clear immorality (fahishah mubayyinah).
2
Examine the Quranic proofs
For ta'rid, verse 2:235 is cited: 'And there is no blame upon you for that which you indicate of proposal to women...' For the house restriction, verse 65:1: 'Do not expel them from their houses, nor shall they leave unless they commit a clear immorality.'
The verses are the primary evidence.
3
Distinguish between direct and indirect proposal
Direct proposal (e.g., 'I want to marry you') is outright forbidden for any woman in iddah. Ta'rid is allusive talk (e.g., 'I wish I had a wife like you') and is allowed only for widows, because they may go out during the day, making private hints possible.
For divorced women, even ta'rid is forbidden by consensus.
4
Understand the exception for leaving the house
The fahishah mubayyinah is interpreted differently: some say it is leaving itself, others say it is adultery or foul language. A divorced woman may leave only for a valid excuse like establishing hadd punishment or if she is harmful to neighbors.
The exception is narrow.
5
Apply the rulings to scenarios
Given a scenario, determine if a direct proposal is made, if ta'rid is used, and if a divorced woman may leave. Use the rules and proofs to justify each answer.
Practice cements the material.

Source Text

(ع)] من الخطبة بكسر الخاء، والمعتدة أعم من أن تكون معتدة عن عتق أو نكاح فاسد أو غيرهما، قيد بالمعتدة؛ لأن الخالية تخطب أي لا ينبغي أن تخطب المعتدة أي معتدة كانت. (مستخلص، عيني) وصح التعريض: [كقوله: أريد التزوج لو معتدة الوفاة لا المطلقة إجماعاً. (ط)] التعريض ذكر شيء يستدل به على شيء آخر لم يذكر، والكناية ذكر الرديف وإرادة المردوف، أي يصح التعريض بالخطبة بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِيمَا عَرَّضْتُمْ بِهِ مِنْ خِطْبَةِ النِّسَاءِ أَوْ أَكُنتُمْ إلى أن قال: ﴿وَلَكِنْ لا تُوَاعِدُوهُنَّ سِرّاً إِلَّا أَنْ تَقُولُوا قَوْلاً مَعْرُوفاً﴾ (البقرة: ٢٣٥)، والتعريض خاص بالمتوفى عنها زوجها فقط؛ لأن التعريض لا يجوز للمطلقة إجماعاً؛ لأنه لا يجوز لها الخروج من منزلها أصلاً، فلا يتمكن من التعريض على وجه لا يقف عليه سواها، فأما المتوفى عنها زوجها يباح لها الخروج نهاراً، فيمكنه التعريض على وجه لا يقف عليه سواها، فالتعريض في الخطبة بأن يقال لها: إنك لجميلة أو صالحة وأشتهي أن يكون لي امرأة مثلك أو يقول: أنا احتاج إلى امرأة صفتها كذا وكذا موافقا صفة المخاطبة ونحو ذلك من الكلام الموهم للخطبة أي الاستنكاح. (مستخلص، فتح) ولا تخرج معتدة الطلاق من بيتها [ لا ليلاً ولا نهاراً حتى تنقضي العدة لو حرة مكلفة. (ط)] بل تعتد في المنزل الذي كان يضاف إليها بالسكنى حال وقوع الطلاق بقوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تُخْرِجُوهُنَّ مِنْ بُيُوتِهِنَّ وَلَا يَخْرُجْنَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَأْتِينَ بِفَاحِشَةٍ مُبَيِّنَةٍ (الطلاق: ۱)، قيل: الفاحشة نفس الخروج، وقيل: الزنا، فليخرجن لإقامة الحدود عليهن، نقل ذلك عن ابن مسعود الله، وقال ابن عباس الهما: أن تكون بذية اللسان فتؤذي جارها فتخرج من منزل الزوج.
And no woman in iddah should be proposed to: [i.e., any woman in iddah, by saying to her: 'I want to marry you.' (Ayni)] From khitbah with kasr on the kha. The mu'taddah is general, whether from emancipation or fasid marriage or others. It is restricted to the mu'taddah because the free woman is proposed to. i.e., it is not appropriate to propose to any woman in iddah. (Mustakhlas, Ayni) And ta'rid is valid: [like saying: 'I want to marry' if she is a widow, not a divorced woman by consensus. (Tahawi)] Ta'rid is mentioning something that indicates something else not mentioned; kinayah is mentioning the secondary and intending the primary. i.e., ta'rid in proposal is valid by the verse: 'And there is no blame upon you for that which you indicate of proposal to women... but do not promise them secretly except that you speak a recognized word.' (2:235). Ta'rid is specific only to the woman whose husband has died, because ta'rid is not permissible for the divorced woman by consensus, because she is not allowed to leave her house at all, so it is not possible to make ta'rid in a way that only she knows. As for the widow, it is permissible for her to go out during the day, so it is possible to make ta'rid in a way that only she knows. Ta'rid in proposal is to say to her: 'You are beautiful or righteous, and I wish I had a wife like you' or 'I need a woman with such and such description matching her description' and similar words that hint at marriage. (Mustakhlas, Fath) And a divorced woman in iddah should not leave her house: [neither night nor day until the iddah ends, if she is a free responsible woman. (Tahawi)] Rather she observes iddah in the house that was attributed to her as residence at the time of divorce, by the verse: 'Do not expel them from their houses, nor shall they leave unless they commit a clear immorality.' (65:1). It is said: the immorality is leaving itself; it is said: it is adultery, so they may go out for the establishment of hadd punishments. This is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) said: The immorality is that she is foul-tongued and harms her neighbor, so she is removed from the husband's house.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage addresses two additional rulings related to iddah. First, it is prohibited to make a direct marriage proposal (khitbah) to any woman in iddah, whether her iddah is from divorce, death, emancipation, or fasid marriage. However, an indirect proposal (ta'rid) is allowed, but only for widows, not for divorced women. The reason is that a divorced woman cannot leave her house at all, so ta'rid cannot be done privately, whereas a widow may go out during the day, allowing for subtle hints. The Quranic verse (2:235) is cited as the basis for ta'rid. Second, a divorced woman in iddah (whether revocable or irrevocable) must remain in the marital home and cannot leave day or night, except if she commits a clear immorality (fahishah mubayyinah). There is a difference of interpretation: some say the immorality is leaving the house itself, others say it is adultery, and still others say it is being foul-tongued. The passage includes opinions from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Abbas. The ruling is based on Quran 65:1.

Key Terms
التعريض (al-ta'rid): An indirect or allusive statement that hints at marriage without explicitly asking.
الفاحشة المبينة (al-fahishah al-mubayyinah): A clear act of immorality that justifies the woman leaving the marital home during iddah; variously interpreted as leaving itself, adultery, or foul language.
العدة (al-iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before remarrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man wishes to marry a woman who is in iddah from a revocable divorce. What is the ruling on proposing to her?
A) Direct proposal is allowed because the iddah is short.
B) Only indirect proposal (ta'rid) is allowed.
C) Both direct and indirect proposal are forbidden.
D) He may propose directly but must wait until after iddah.

Key Takeaway
Direct proposal to any woman in iddah is haram; indirect hints are only for widows. A divorced woman must remain in her home unless she commits a clear immorality.

The Obligation of Ihdad: Who Must Mourn?
Ruling with proof and intra-madhhab dispute on ihdad obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for ihdad being wajib and identify which women are exempted, including the intra-Hanafi dispute on non-Muslims.

Core Idea
Ihdad is wajib only for adult Muslim women in iddah of death or irrevocable divorce.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies the obligation of ihdad (abstaining from adornment) during iddah. The matn lists exceptions, and the commentary expands on conditions (adulthood, Islam) and notes a dispute among Hanafi imams regarding non-Muslim women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
The matn states that ihdad is required for a woman who is adult (balighah) and Muslim (muslimah). Confirm that these two conditions are essential for the obligation.
The commentary explicitly says: 'This mourning is obligatory on her under condition of adulthood and Islam.'
2
List the women exempted from ihdad
The matn excludes: (1) a woman in iddah of emancipation (um walad), (2) a woman in iddah of an invalid marriage. The commentary adds: a woman in iddah of revocable divorce, a non-Muslim, and a minor.
The common reason: these women have not lost the 'blessing of marriage' (ni'mat al-nikah).
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on non-Muslims
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that ihdad is not obligatory on a non-Muslim woman. The 'three' (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Imam al-Shafi'i) hold it is obligatory due to general texts. Understand the proof for each side.
The Hanafi response: ihdad is an act of worship that requires faith (iman); Quran 7:32 indicates permissibility of adornment as the original principle.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later Hanafi authorities preferred Abu Hanifa's view, so the relied-upon position is that ihdad is not obligatory on a non-Muslim woman. Note the practical consequence.
If a non-Muslim converts during iddah, ihdad becomes wajib for the remaining period, by agreement.

ولا تخطب معتدة: [ أي معتدة كانت بأن يقول لها: إني أريد أن أنكحك. (ع)] من الخطبة بكسر الخاء، والمعتدة أعم من أن تكون معتدة عن عتق أو نكاح فاسد أو غيرهما، قيد بالمعتدة؛ لأن الخالية تخطب أي لا ينبغي أن تخطب المعتدة أي معتدة كانت. (مستخلص، عيني)
وصح التعريض: [كقوله: أريد التزوج لو معتدة الوفاة لا المطلقة إجماعاً. (ط)] التعريض ذكر شيء يستدل به على شيء آخر لم يذكر، والكناية ذكر الرديف وإرادة المردوف، أي يصح التعريض بالخطبة بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِيمَا عَرَّضْتُمْ بِهِ مِنْ خِطْبَةِ النِّسَاءِ أَوْ أَكُنتُمْ إلى أن قال: ﴿وَلَكِنْ لا تُوَاعِدُوهُنَّ سِرّاً إِلَّا أَنْ تَقُولُوا قَوْلاً مَعْرُوفاً﴾ (البقرة: ٢٣٥)، والتعريض خاص بالمتوفى عنها زوجها فقط؛ لأن التعريض لا يجوز للمطلقة إجماعاً؛ لأنه لا يجوز لها الخروج من منزلها أصلاً، فلا يتمكن من التعريض على وجه لا يقف عليه سواها، فأما المتوفى عنها زوجها يباح لها الخروج نهاراً، فيمكنه التعريض على وجه لا يقف عليه سواها، فالتعريض في الخطبة بأن يقال لها: إنك لجميلة أو صالحة وأشتهي أن يكون لي امرأة مثلك أو يقول: أنا احتاج إلى امرأة صفتها كذا وكذا موافقا صفة المخاطبة ونحو ذلك من الكلام الموهم للخطبة أي الاستنكاح. (مستخلص، فتح)
Book of Divorce. Explanation of the Iddah Mourning and Its Rulings. And wearing safflower-dyed and saffron-dyed clothing if she is an adult Muslim, even if a slave woman; not for the iddah of emancipation or invalid marriage. So it is not obligatory on the dhimmi woman. [Commentary...] And do not propose to a woman in iddah; indirect proposal is valid. [Commentary...]
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq with its commentary explains the rules of mourning (ihdad) for a woman in iddah. The matn states that wearing dyed clothing is forbidden for an adult Muslim woman in iddah, even if she is a slave. However, this obligation does not apply to a woman observing iddah due to emancipation (um walad) or due to an invalid marriage. The commentary clarifies that ihdad is obligatory under conditions of adulthood and Islam; it is not obligatory on a non-Muslim or a minor. If a non-Muslim converts during iddah, ihdad becomes obligatory for the remaining period. The commentary notes that the three (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Imam Shafi'i) hold that ihdad is obligatory on a non-Muslim woman too, based on general texts, but the Hanafi position restricts it to Muslim women. The ruling also excludes a woman whose iddah is due to a revocable divorce or an invalid marriage because the blessing of marriage is still present. Then the text forbids direct proposal (khitbah) to any woman in iddah, whether due to divorce, emancipation, or invalid marriage. However, indirect proposal (ta'rid) is allowed, but only for a widow, not for a divorced woman, because a widow may go out during the day allowing opportunity for indirect speech. The Quranic verse (2:235) is cited as proof for the permissibility of ta'rid.

Key Terms
الحداد (al-ihdad): Abstaining from all adornment, including wearing perfumed or colored clothes, during the iddah period to express mourning.
المعصفر (al-mu'asfar): Cloth dyed with safflower, which is considered an adornment and must be avoided during ihdad.
المزعفر (al-muza'far): Cloth dyed with saffron, also an adornment to be avoided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following women is NOT required to observe ihdad?
A) A Muslim adult widow
B) A Muslim adult woman divorced irrevocably
C) A non-Muslim adult widow
D) A Muslim adult woman in iddah after an invalid marriage

Key Takeaway
Ihdad is wajib only for adult Muslim women in iddah of death or irrevocable divorce; non-Muslims, minors, and those in iddah of revocable divorce or invalid marriage are exempt.

Proposing to a Woman in Iddah: Direct vs Indirect
Ruling with proof on proposal restrictions during iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible indirect proposals (ta'rid) and prohibited direct proposals (khitbah) to women in iddah, and state the exception for widows.

Core Idea
Direct proposal to any woman in iddah is haram, but indirect proposals are permissible only for widows.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq establishes the prohibition of directly proposing marriage (khitbah) to any woman in iddah, regardless of the type of iddah. It then explains that indirect proposal (ta'rid) is valid, but only for a widow, due to her ability to go out during the day.

Guided Path
1
Understand the blanket prohibition of khitbah
The matn says: 'Do not propose to a woman in iddah.' The commentary clarifies this applies to any woman in iddah, whether from divorce, emancipation, or invalid marriage.
The word 'mu'taddah' is general.
2
Define ta'rid (indirect proposal)
The commentary defines ta'rid as hinting without explicit mention of marriage. Examples: praising the woman or describing desired qualities.
Contrast with kinayah (metonymy) which is similar.
3
Identify the exception for widows
Ta'rid is allowed only for a widow, not for a divorced woman. The reason given is that a widow may leave her home during the day, enabling private communication; a divorced woman is confined.
There is consensus (ijma') that ta'rid is not permissible for a divorced woman.
4
Apply the Quranic proof
The commentator cites Surah al-Baqarah 2:235 as the basis for the permissibility of ta'rid. The verse explicitly states there is no sin in indirect proposals.
The verse also prohibits secret promises (muwa'adah sirran).

(ع)] أي هذا الحداد واجب عليها بشرط البلوغ والإسلام، فلا يجب على الكافرة وإن أبانها مسلم أو مات عنها، إلا إذا أسلمت في خلال العدة وجب عليها في الباقي، وقالت الثلاثة عليها الحداد؛ لإطلاق النصوص، ولا على الصبية؛ لأنها غير مخاطبة اتفاقاً. الخطبة (al-khitbah): Direct proposal for marriage, explicitly asking for her hand.
الكناية (al-kinayah): Metonymy using a related term to imply the intended meaning; similar to ta'rid but distinct.

8 min
Confinement of Divorced and Widowed Women During Iddah
Ruling on iddah residence with proof and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the residence obligations of a divorced woman and a widow during iddah, and identify the exceptions that permit leaving the home.

Core Idea
A divorced woman must never leave the marital home; a widow may go out by day for necessities.

The waiting period (iddah) after divorce or widowhood carries specific spatial obligations. The Hanafi school imposes a strict duty on divorced women to remain in the marital home day and night, while widows have slightly more flexibility due to their financial independence. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the Quran, and the key exceptions that arise from necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Separate the rulings for a divorced woman (whether revocable or irrevocable) and a widow. Note the basic rule: no leaving at all for the divorced; daytime leaving permitted for the widow.
The divorced woman's obligation is stricter because her nafaqah (maintenance) is still due from the husband, so she does not need to work.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof
Examine Surah al-Talaq (65:1): 'Do not expel them from their houses, nor let them go out, unless they commit a clear immorality.' Understand how the Hanafis derive the absolute prohibition from the negative imperative and discuss the different interpretations of 'fahishah'.
The word 'لا يخرجن' is a emphatic prohibition, indicating wujub.
3
Understand the exceptions for necessity
List the valid excuses that permit both types of women to leave: fear for life or property, collapse of the house, inability to pay rent, etc. Note that moving is only to another home where iddah continues.
The exception is tightly defined to prevent abuse.
4
Note intra-Hanafi differences
Observe that Imam Muhammad differs on the widow's night-time permission: he allows less than half the night, while the majority of Hanafis allow part of the night. This is a minor ikhtilaf within the school.
The mufta bihi follows the majority view.
5
Apply to special scenarios
Consider cases like a minor girl, a non-Muslim woman, or a woman whose husband is absent. The passage provides specific adjustments: the minor may leave if the divorce is irrevocable; the non-Muslim is not addressed by shar'i rulings but the husband may restrain her to protect his lineage.
These scenarios show the operation of 'illah (effective cause) in Hanafi fiqh.
